"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Absolute_zero"" title=""Absolute zero"">absolute zero</a>"|"
A theoretical condition concerning a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physical_system"" title=""Physical system"">system</a> at the lowest limit of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thermodynamic_temperature"" title=""Thermodynamic temperature"">thermodynamic temperature</a> scale, or zero <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#kelvin""><span title=""See entry on this page at § kelvin"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">kelvins</span></a>, at which the system does not emit or absorb energy (i.e. all <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atoms</span></a> are at rest). By extrapolating the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ideal_gas_law""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ideal gas law"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ideal gas law</span></a>, the internationally agreed-upon value for absolute zero has been determined as −273.15&#160;°C (−459.67&#160;°F; 0.00&#160;K).
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Absorbance"" title=""Absorbance"">absorbance</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Absorption_(chemistry)"" title=""Absorption (chemistry)"">absorption</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;The physical or chemical process by which a substance in one <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#state_of_matter""><span title=""See entry on this page at § state of matter"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">state</span></a> becomes incorporated into and retained by another substance of a different state. Absorption differs from <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#adsorption""><span title=""See entry on this page at § adsorption"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">adsorption</span></a> in that the first substance permeates the entire bulk of the second substance, rather than just adhering to the surface.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Absorption_(electromagnetic_radiation)"" title=""Absorption (electromagnetic radiation)"">process</a> by which matter (typically <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electrons</span></a> bound in atoms) takes up the energy of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electromagnetic_radiation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electromagnetic radiation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electromagnetic radiation</span></a> and transforms it into any of various types of internal energy, such as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thermal_energy"" title=""Thermal energy"">thermal energy</a>. This type of absorption is the principle on which <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#spectrophotometry""><span title=""See entry on this page at § spectrophotometry"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">spectrophotometry</span></a> is based.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abundance_(chemistry)"" title=""Abundance (chemistry)"">abundance</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Accuracy"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Accuracy"">accuracy</a>"|"
How close a measured value is to the actual or true value. Compare <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#precision""><span title=""See entry on this page at § precision"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">precision</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acid"" title=""Acid"">acid</a>"|"
A compound which, when dissolved in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#water""><span title=""See entry on this page at § water"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">water</span></a>, gives a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#pH""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pH"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pH</span></a> of less than 7.0, or donates a hydrogen ion.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acid_anhydride"" title=""Acid anhydride"">acid anhydride</a>"|"
A compound with two <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acyl_group"" title=""Acyl group"">acyl groups</a> bound to a single oxygen atom.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acid_dissociation_constant"" title=""Acid dissociation constant"">acid dissociation constant</a> (K<sub>a</sub>)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>acid ionization constant</b> or <b>acidity constant</b>.</span></p>
A quantitative measure of the strength of an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#acid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § acid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">acid</span></a> in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solution</span></a> expressed as an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#equilibrium_constant""><span title=""See entry on this page at § equilibrium constant"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">equilibrium constant</span></a> for a chemical <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#dissociation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § dissociation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">dissociation</span></a> reaction in the context of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#acid-base_reaction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § acid-base reaction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">acid-base reactions</span></a>. It is often given as its base-10 cologarithm, <i>pK<sub>a</sub></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Actinoid"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Actinoid"">actinides</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>actinoids</b>.</span></p>
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#period""><span title=""See entry on this page at § period"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">periodic</span></a> series of metallic elements with atomic numbers 89 to 103, from <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Actinium"" title=""Actinium"">actinium</a> through <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lawrencium"" title=""Lawrencium"">lawrencium</a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Activated_complex"" title=""Activated complex"">activated complex</a>"|"
A structure that forms because of a collision between molecules while new bonds are formed.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Activation_energy"" title=""Activation energy"">activation energy</a>"|"
The minimum <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#energy""><span title=""See entry on this page at § energy"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">energy</span></a> which must be available to a chemical system with potential <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#reactant""><span title=""See entry on this page at § reactant"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">reactants</span></a> in order to result in a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical reaction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical reaction</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Activity_series"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Activity series"">activity series</a>"|"
See <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#reactivity_series""><span title=""See entry on this page at § reactivity series"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">reactivity series</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Actual_yield"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Actual yield"">actual yield</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open-chain_compound"" title=""Open-chain compound"">acyclic</a>"|"
Containing only linear structures of atoms (particularly in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#hydrocarbon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hydrocarbon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hydrocarbons</span></a>).
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Addition_reaction"" title=""Addition reaction"">addition reaction</a>"|"
In organic chemistry, when two or more molecules combine to make a larger one.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adhesion"" title=""Adhesion"">adhesion</a>"|"
The tendency of dissimilar particles or surfaces to cling to one another as a result of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#intermolecular_force""><span title=""See entry on this page at § intermolecular force"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">intermolecular forces</span></a>. Contrast <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#cohesion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cohesion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cohesion</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adsorption"" title=""Adsorption"">adsorption</a>"|"
The chemical <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#adhesion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § adhesion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">adhesion</span></a> of atoms, ions, or molecules of one substance (either a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#gas""><span title=""See entry on this page at § gas"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gas</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquid</span></a>, or dissolved <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solid</span></a>) to the surface of another substance, resulting in a film of the first substance being weakly bonded to the interface between the two substances. Adsorption differs from <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#absorption""><span title=""See entry on this page at § absorption"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">absorption</span></a> in that it is exclusively a surface phenomenon, while absorption involves entire volumes of materials.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aeration"" title=""Aeration"">aeration</a>"|"
The mixing of air into a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquid</span></a> or a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solid</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alcohol"" title=""Alcohol"">alcohol</a>"|"
Any <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#organic_compound""><span title=""See entry on this page at § organic compound"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">organic compound</span></a> consisting of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#hydroxyl""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hydroxyl"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hydroxyl</span></a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#functional_group""><span title=""See entry on this page at § functional group"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">functional group</span></a> attached to a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturated_and_unsaturated_compounds"" title=""Saturated and unsaturated compounds"">saturated</a> carbon atom.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aldehyde"" title=""Aldehyde"">aldehyde</a>"|"
Any organic compound consisting of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#carbonyl_group""><span title=""See entry on this page at § carbonyl group"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">carbonyl group</span></a> attached to a hydrogen atom and any other <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Side_chain"" title=""Side chain"">R-group</a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alkali_metal"" title=""Alkali metal"">alkali metal</a>"|"
Any of the metallic <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#element""><span title=""See entry on this page at § element"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">elements</span></a> belonging to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#group""><span title=""See entry on this page at § group"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Group 1</span></a> of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#periodic_table""><span title=""See entry on this page at § periodic table"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">periodic table</span></a>: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithium"" title=""Lithium"">lithium</a> (Li), <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sodium"" title=""Sodium"">sodium</a> (Na), <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Potassium"" title=""Potassium"">potassium</a> (K), <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rubidium"" title=""Rubidium"">rubidium</a> (Rb), <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caesium"" title=""Caesium"">caesium</a> (Cs), and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francium"" title=""Francium"">francium</a> (Fr).
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alkaline_earth_metal"" title=""Alkaline earth metal"">alkaline earth metal</a>"|"
Any of the metallic <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#element""><span title=""See entry on this page at § element"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">elements</span></a> belonging to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#group""><span title=""See entry on this page at § group"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Group 2</span></a> of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#periodic_table""><span title=""See entry on this page at § periodic table"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">periodic table</span></a>: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beryllium"" title=""Beryllium"">beryllium</a> (Be), <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnesium"" title=""Magnesium"">magnesium</a> (Mg), <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calcium"" title=""Calcium"">calcium</a> (Ca), <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strontium"" title=""Strontium"">strontium</a> (Sr), <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barium"" title=""Barium"">barium</a> (Ba), and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radium"" title=""Radium"">radium</a> (Ra).
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alkane"" title=""Alkane"">alkane</a>"|"
Any saturated acyclic <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#hydrocarbon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hydrocarbon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hydrocarbon</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alkene"" title=""Alkene"">alkene</a>"|"
An unsaturated <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#hydrocarbon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hydrocarbon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hydrocarbon</span></a> containing at least one pair of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#double_bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § double bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">double-bonded</span></a> carbons.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alkyl_group"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Alkyl group"">alkyl group</a>"|"
A functional group consisting of an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#alkane""><span title=""See entry on this page at § alkane"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">alkane</span></a> missing a hydrogen atom.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alkyne"" title=""Alkyne"">alkyne</a>"|"
An unsaturated <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#hydrocarbon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hydrocarbon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hydrocarbon</span></a> containing at least one pair of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#triple_bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § triple bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">triple-bonded</span></a> carbons.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allomer"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Allomer"">allomer</a>"|"
A substance that differs in chemical composition but has the same <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#crystal""><span title=""See entry on this page at § crystal"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">crystalline</span></a> structure as another substance.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allotrope"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Allotrope"">allotrope</a>"|"
Elements that can have different structures (and therefore different forms), such as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon"" title=""Carbon"">carbon</a> (<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diamonds"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Diamonds"">diamonds</a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graphite"" title=""Graphite"">graphite</a>, and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fullerene"" title=""Fullerene"">fullerene</a>).
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alloy"" title=""Alloy"">alloy</a>"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mixture""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mixture"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mixture</span></a> of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#metal""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metal"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">metals</span></a> or of a metal and another <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#element""><span title=""See entry on this page at § element"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">element</span></a> which in combination exhibit a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#metallic_bonding""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metallic bonding"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">metallic bonding</span></a> character. Common examples include <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bronze"" title=""Bronze"">bronze</a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brass"" title=""Brass"">brass</a>, and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pewter"" title=""Pewter"">pewter</a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amalgam_(chemistry)"" title=""Amalgam (chemistry)"">amalgam</a>"|"
Any <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#alloy""><span title=""See entry on this page at § alloy"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">alloy</span></a> of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercury_(element)"" title=""Mercury (element)"">mercury</a> with another <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#metal""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metal"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">metal</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amount_of_substance"" title=""Amount of substance"">amount of substance</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>enplethy</b>, <b>chemical amount</b>, or simply <b>amount</b>.</span></p>
The number of discrete particles (such as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecule"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molecules</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atoms</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ions</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electrons</span></a>, or any other atomic-scale entity) in a given sample of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#matter""><span title=""See entry on this page at § matter"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">matter</span></a>, divided by the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#avogadro&#39;s_number""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Avogadro&#39;s number"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Avogadro constant</span></a>. The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#sI""><span title=""See entry on this page at § SI"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">SI</span></a> base unit for amount of substance is the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mole</span></a> (mol).
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Analyte"" title=""Analyte"">analyte</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Analytical_chemistry"" title=""Analytical chemistry"">analytical chemistry</a>"|"
The branch of chemistry which studies and makes use of instruments and methods to separate, quantify, and identify chemical substances, both by classical <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#wet_chemistry""><span title=""See entry on this page at § wet chemistry"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">wet chemistry</span></a> techniques such as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#precipitation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § precipitation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">precipitation</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#extraction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § extraction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">extraction</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#distillation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § distillation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">distillation</span></a>, and observational analysis, and by modern instrumental techniques such as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chromatography""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chromatography"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chromatography</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#spectroscopy""><span title=""See entry on this page at § spectroscopy"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">spectroscopy</span></a>, and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electrochemistry""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electrochemistry"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electrochemistry</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anion"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Anion"">anion</a>"|"
A negatively charged <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ion</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anode"" title=""Anode"">anode</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;An <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electrode""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electrode"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electrode</span></a> through which the conventional <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electric_current"" title=""Electric current"">electric current</a> (the flow of positive charges) enters into a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#polarity""><span title=""See entry on this page at § polarity"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">polarized</span></a> electrical circuit.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;The wire or plate of an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electrochemical_cell""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electrochemical cell"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electrochemical cell</span></a> having an excess positive charge. Negatively charged <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#anion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § anion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">anions</span></a> always move toward the anode. Contrast <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#cathode""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cathode"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cathode</span></a></i>.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aqueous_solution"" title=""Aqueous solution"">aqueous solution</a>"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solution</span></a> in which the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solvent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solvent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solvent</span></a> is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#water""><span title=""See entry on this page at § water"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">water</span></a>. It is denoted in chemical equations by appending <i>(aq)</i> to a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_formula""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical formula"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical formula</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aromaticity"" title=""Aromaticity"">aromaticity</a>"|"
A chemical property of conjugated rings of atoms, such as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#benzene""><span title=""See entry on this page at § benzene"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">benzene</span></a>, which results in unusually high stability. Such rings are said to be <i>aromatic</i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arrow_pushing"" title=""Arrow pushing"">arrow pushing</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aryl"" title=""Aryl"">aryl</a>"|"
Any <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#functional_group""><span title=""See entry on this page at § functional group"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">functional group</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#substituent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § substituent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">substituent</span></a> derived from an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#aromaticity""><span title=""See entry on this page at § aromaticity"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">aromatic ring</span></a>, such as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phenyl"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Phenyl"">phenyl</a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naphthyl"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Naphthyl"">naphthyl</a>. The symbol <i>Ar</i> is often used as a placeholder for a generic aryl group in structural diagrams.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atom"" title=""Atom"">atom</a>"|"
A chemical element in its smallest form, made up of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#proton""><span title=""See entry on this page at § proton"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">protons</span></a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#neutron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § neutron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">neutrons</span></a> within the nucleus and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electrons</span></a> circling the nucleus.
<div class=""thumb tright""><div class=""thumbinner"" style=""width:222px;""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Atom-struc.svg"" class=""image""><img alt="""" src=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Atom-struc.svg/220px-Atom-struc.svg.png"" decoding=""async"" width=""220"" height=""129"" class=""thumbimage"" srcset=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Atom-struc.svg/330px-Atom-struc.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Atom-struc.svg/440px-Atom-struc.svg.png 2x"" data-file-width=""374"" data-file-height=""219"" /></a>  <div class=""thumbcaption""><div class=""magnify""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Atom-struc.svg"" class=""internal"" title=""Enlarge""></a></div>An <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atom</span></a> with <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#proton""><span title=""See entry on this page at § proton"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">protons</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#neutron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § neutron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">neutrons</span></a>, and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electrons</span></a> labelled</div></div></div>"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_mass"" title=""Atomic mass"">atomic mass</a>"|"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mass""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mass"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mass</span></a> of an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atom</span></a>, typically expressed in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#unified_atomic_mass_unit""><span title=""See entry on this page at § unified atomic mass unit"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">unified atomic mass units</span></a> and nearly equivalent to the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mass_number""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mass number"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mass number</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_mass_unit"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Atomic mass unit"">atomic mass unit</a>"|"
See <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#unified_atomic_mass_unit""><span title=""See entry on this page at § unified atomic mass unit"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">unified atomic mass unit</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_number"" title=""Atomic number"">atomic number</a> (Z)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>proton number</b>.</span></p>
The number of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#proton""><span title=""See entry on this page at § proton"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">protons</span></a> found in the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#nucleus""><span title=""See entry on this page at § nucleus"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">nucleus</span></a> of an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atom</span></a> of a given <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#element""><span title=""See entry on this page at § element"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical element</span></a>. It is identical to the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#charge_number""><span title=""See entry on this page at § charge number"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">charge number</span></a> of the nucleus and is used in the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#periodic_table""><span title=""See entry on this page at § periodic table"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">periodic table</span></a> to uniquely identify each chemical element.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_orbital"" title=""Atomic orbital"">atomic orbital</a>"|"
Any region in which one or more <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electrons</span></a> may be found in an individual <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atom</span></a> (as opposed to that within <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecular_orbital""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecular orbital"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">a molecule</span></a>).
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_radius"" title=""Atomic radius"">atomic radius</a>"|"

"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avogadro%27s_law"" title=""Avogadro&#39;s law"">Avogadro's law</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avogadro%27s_number"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Avogadro&#39;s number"">Avogadro's number</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>Avogadro constant</b>.</span></p>
The number of discrete constituent particles (such as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecule"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molecules</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atoms</span></a>, or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ions</span></a>) in one <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mole</span></a> of a substance, defined as exactly 6.02214076<span style=""margin:0 .15em 0 .25em"">×</span>10<sup><span style=""white-space:nowrap"">23</span></sup> such particles.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azeotrope"" title=""Azeotrope"">azeotrope</a>"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mixture""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mixture"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mixture</span></a> of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquids</span></a> whose composition is unchanged by <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#distillation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § distillation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">distillation</span></a>."
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barometer"" title=""Barometer"">barometer</a>"|"
A device used to measure atmospheric pressure.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Base_(chemistry)"" title=""Base (chemistry)"">base</a>"|"
A substance that accepts a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#proton""><span title=""See entry on this page at § proton"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">proton</span></a> and has a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#pH""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pH"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pH</span></a> above 7.0. A common example is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sodium_hydroxide"" title=""Sodium hydroxide"">sodium hydroxide</a> (NaOH).
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Base_anhydride"" title=""Base anhydride"">base anhydride</a>"|"
Oxides of group I and II metal elements.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beaker_(glassware)"" title=""Beaker (glassware)"">beaker</a>"|"
A cylindrical vessel or container with a flat bottom, most commonly a type of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glassware"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Glassware"">glassware</a>, widely used in laboratories for a variety of purposes, such as preparing, holding, containing, collecting, or volumetrically measuring chemicals, samples, or solutions, or as a chamber in which a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical reaction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical reaction</span></a> occurs. Beakers are distinguished from <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#flask""><span title=""See entry on this page at § flask"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">flasks</span></a> by having straight rather than sloping sides; most beakers also have a small spout in the rim to aid pouring.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beer%E2%80%93Lambert_law"" title=""Beer–Lambert law"">Beer–Lambert law</a>"|"

The study of the chemistry of biological systems and organisms.

"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boiling"" title=""Boiling"">boiling</a>"|"
See <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#vaporization""><span title=""See entry on this page at § vaporization"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">vaporization</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boiling_point"" title=""Boiling point"">boiling point</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>vaporization point</b>.</span></p>
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#temperature""><span title=""See entry on this page at § temperature"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">temperature</span></a> at which a substance changes <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#state_of_matter""><span title=""See entry on this page at § state of matter"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">state</span></a> from a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquid</span></a> to a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#gas""><span title=""See entry on this page at § gas"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gas</span></a> (or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#vapor""><span title=""See entry on this page at § vapor"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">vapor</span></a>). It depends on <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#pressure""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pressure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pressure</span></a> and is usually specified for a given substance under <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#standard_temperature_and_pressure""><span title=""See entry on this page at § standard temperature and pressure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">standard conditions</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boiling-point_elevation"" title=""Boiling-point elevation"">boiling-point elevation</a>"|"
the process where the boiling point is elevated by adding a substance
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_bond"" title=""Chemical bond"">bond</a>"|"
Any persistent attraction between <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atoms</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ions</span></a>, or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecule"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molecules</span></a> that enables the formation of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#compound""><span title=""See entry on this page at § compound"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical compounds</span></a>. Bonds are created as a result of a wide variety of electrochemical forces, whose strengths can vary considerably; they are broken when these forces are overcome by other forces. The types, strengths, and quantities of bonds holding together chemical substances dictate the structure and bulk properties of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#matter""><span title=""See entry on this page at § matter"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">matter</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boyle%27s_law"" title=""Boyle&#39;s law"">Boyle's law</a>"|"
For a given mass of gas at constant temperature, the volume varies inversely with the pressure.
"

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Br%C3%B8nsted%E2%80%93Lowry_acid%E2%80%93base_theory"" title=""Brønsted–Lowry acid–base theory"">Brønsted–Lowry acid</a>"|"
Any chemical species that readily donates a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#proton""><span title=""See entry on this page at § proton"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">proton</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Br%C3%B8nsted%E2%80%93Lowry_acid%E2%80%93base_theory"" title=""Brønsted–Lowry acid–base theory"">Brønsted–Lowry acid–base reaction</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Br%C3%B8nsted%E2%80%93Lowry_acid%E2%80%93base_theory"" title=""Brønsted–Lowry acid–base theory"">Brønsted–Lowry base</a>"|"
Any chemical species that readily accepts a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#proton""><span title=""See entry on this page at § proton"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">proton</span></a>.

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buffered_solution"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Buffered solution"">buffered solution</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also simply called a <b>buffer</b>.</span></p>
An <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#aqueous_solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § aqueous solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">aqueous solution</span></a> consisting of a weak <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#acid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § acid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">acid</span></a> and its <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#conjugate_base""><span title=""See entry on this page at § conjugate base"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">conjugate base</span></a> or a weak <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#base""><span title=""See entry on this page at § base"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">base</span></a> and its <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#conjugate_acid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § conjugate acid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">conjugate acid</span></a> that resists changes in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#pH""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pH"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pH</span></a> when strong acids or bases are added.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bumping_(chemistry)"" title=""Bumping (chemistry)"">bumping</a>"|"
A phenomenon in which a homogeneous liquid raised to its <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#boiling_point""><span title=""See entry on this page at § boiling point"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">boiling point</span></a> becomes <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#superheating""><span title=""See entry on this page at § superheating"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">superheated</span></a> and, upon <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#nucleation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § nucleation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">nucleation</span></a>, rapidly boils to the gas phase, resulting in a violent expulsion of the liquid from the container; in extreme cases, the container itself may shatter. Frequent stirring, the use of an appropriate container, and the use of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boiling_chip"" title=""Boiling chip"">boiling chips</a> can help prevent bumping.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bung"" title=""Bung"">bung</a>"|"

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burette"" title=""Burette"">burette</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also spelled <b>buret</b>.</span></p>
Glassware used to dispense specific amounts of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquid</span></a> when precision is necessary (e.g. during <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#titration""><span title=""See entry on this page at § titration"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">titrations</span></a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#resource_dependent_reaction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § resource dependent reaction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">resource-dependent reactions</span></a>)."
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calorimeter"" title=""Calorimeter"">calorimeter</a>"|"
A device used to measure <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#heat""><span title=""See entry on this page at § heat"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">heat</span></a>.
"
