"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbocation"" title=""Carbocation"">carbocation</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catalyst"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Catalyst"">catalyst</a>"|"
Any element or compound that facilitates an increase in the speed of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical reaction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical reaction</span></a> but which is not consumed or destroyed during the reaction. It is considered both a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#reactant""><span title=""See entry on this page at § reactant"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">reactant</span></a> and a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#product""><span title=""See entry on this page at § product"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">product</span></a> of the reaction.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cathode"" title=""Cathode"">cathode</a>"|"
An <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electrode""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electrode"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electrode</span></a> from which the conventional <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electric_current"" title=""Electric current"">electric current</a> (the flow of positive charges) exits a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#polarity""><span title=""See entry on this page at § polarity"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">polarized</span></a> electrical circuit. Positively charged <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#cation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cations</span></a> always move toward the cathode, though the cathode's polarity can be positive or negative depending on the type of electrical device and how it is being operated. Contrast <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#anode""><span title=""See entry on this page at § anode"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">anode</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cation"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Cation"">cation</a>"|"
A positively charged <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ion</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centrifugation"" title=""Centrifugation"">centrifugation</a>"|"
A laboratory technique which involves the application of centrifugal force to separate particles from a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solution</span></a> according to their size, shape, and density. Larger and/or denser substances migrate away from the axis of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#centrifuge""><span title=""See entry on this page at § centrifuge"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">centrifuge</span></a>, while smaller and/or less dense substances migrate towards the axis.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centrifuge"" title=""Centrifuge"">centrifuge</a>"|"
A device used to separate substances based on size, shape, and density by <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#centrifugation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § centrifugation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">centrifugation</span></a>, or the rotation of vessels containing the substances around a centred axis at extremely high velocities.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resting_potential"" title=""Resting potential"">cell potential</a>"|"
The force in a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galvanic_cell"" title=""Galvanic cell"">galvanic cell</a> that pulls electrons through a reducing agent to an oxidizing agent.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chain_reaction"" title=""Chain reaction"">chain reaction</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charge_number"" title=""Charge number"">charge number</a>"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantification_(science)"" title=""Quantification (science)"">quantized</a> value of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electric_charge""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electric charge"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electric charge</span></a> calculated as the electric charge in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#coulomb""><span title=""See entry on this page at § coulomb"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">coulombs</span></a> divided by the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elementary_charge"" title=""Elementary charge"">elementary-charge</a> constant, or <i>z = q/e</i>. Charge numbers for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ions</span></a> are denoted in superscript (e.g. Na<sup>+</sup> indicates a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sodium"" title=""Sodium"">sodium</a> ion with a charge number of positive one). <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atomic_number""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atomic number"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Atomic numbers</span></a> are charge numbers of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#nucleus""><span title=""See entry on this page at § nucleus"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atomic nuclei</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles%27s_law"" title=""Charles&#39;s law"">Charles's law</a>"|"
When the pressure on a sample of a dry gas is held constant, the Kelvin temperature is directly proportional to its volume.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chelating_agent"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Chelating agent"">chelating agent</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chelation"" title=""Chelation"">chelation</a>"|"
A type of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bonding</span></a> involving the formation of two separate <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#coordinate_covalent_bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § coordinate covalent bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">coordinate covalent bonds</span></a> between a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#denticity""><span title=""See entry on this page at § denticity"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">polydentate</span></a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ligand""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ligand"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ligand</span></a> and a single central <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#metal""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metal"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">metal</span></a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ion</span></a>. The ligand is usually an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#organic_compound""><span title=""See entry on this page at § organic compound"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">organic compound</span></a> called a <i>chelant</i> or <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chelating_agent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chelating agent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chelating agent</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_composition"" title=""Chemical composition"">chemical composition</a>"|"
The identity and relative number of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#element""><span title=""See entry on this page at § element"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">elements</span></a> that make up a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#compound""><span title=""See entry on this page at § compound"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical compound</span></a>, which can often be expressed with a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_formula""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical formula"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical formula</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_decomposition"" title=""Chemical decomposition"">chemical decomposition</a>"|"
The breakdown of a single particle or entity (such as a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecule"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molecule</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#reactive_intermediate""><span title=""See entry on this page at § reactive intermediate"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">reactive intermediate</span></a>) into two or more fragments, or a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical reaction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical reaction</span></a> in which two or more <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#product""><span title=""See entry on this page at § product"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">products</span></a> are formed from a single <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#reactant""><span title=""See entry on this page at § reactant"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">reactant</span></a>. Contrast <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_synthesis""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical synthesis"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical synthesis</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_formula"" title=""Chemical formula"">chemical formula</a>"|"
Any of various means of concisely displaying information about the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_composition""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical composition"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical composition</span></a> of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#compound""><span title=""See entry on this page at § compound"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">compound</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecule"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molecule</span></a> using letters, numbers, and/or typographical symbols. Chemical formulas, such as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#empirical_formula""><span title=""See entry on this page at § empirical formula"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">empirical</span></a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecular_formula""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecular formula"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molecular formulas</span></a>, can only indicate the identities and numerical proportions of the atoms in a compound and are therefore more limited in descriptive power than <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_nomenclature""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical nomenclature"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical names</span></a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#structural_formula""><span title=""See entry on this page at § structural formula"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">structural formulas</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_law"" title=""Chemical law"">chemical law</a>"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physical_law"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Physical law"">law of nature</a> relevant to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemistry""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemistry"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemistry</span></a>, such as the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#law_of_conservation_of_mass""><span title=""See entry on this page at § law of conservation of mass"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">law of conservation of mass</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_nomenclature"" title=""Chemical nomenclature"">chemical nomenclature</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_process"" title=""Chemical process"">chemical process</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;Any method or means of changing one or more <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_species""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical species"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemicals</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#compound""><span title=""See entry on this page at § compound"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical compounds</span></a> in any way, either naturally or artificially, spontaneously or by the actions of external forces.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;In <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_engineering"" title=""Chemical engineering"">chemical engineering</a>, any method used on an industrial scale (especially in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manufacturing"" title=""Manufacturing"">manufacturing</a>) to change the composition of one or more chemicals or materials.</dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_reaction"" title=""Chemical reaction"">chemical reaction</a>"|"
The change of one or more <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_substance""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical substance"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">substances</span></a> into one or more different substances.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_species"" title=""Chemical species"">chemical species</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also simply called a <b>chemical</b>.</span></p>
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_substance""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical substance"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical substance</span></a> or ensemble of substances composed of chemically identical <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecular_entity"" title=""Molecular entity"">molecular entities</a> which can explore the same set of molecular energy levels on a characteristic or delineated time scale.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_substance"" title=""Chemical substance"">chemical substance</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>pure substance</b> or simply <b>substance</b>.</span></p>
A form of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#matter""><span title=""See entry on this page at § matter"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">matter</span></a> that has constant <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_composition""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical composition"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical composition</span></a> and characteristic <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#physical_property""><span title=""See entry on this page at § physical property"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">properties</span></a> and which cannot be separated into simpler components by purely physical methods (i.e. without breaking <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical bonds</span></a>). It is often called a <i>pure substance</i> to distinguish it from a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mixture""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mixture"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mixture</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_synthesis"" title=""Chemical synthesis"">chemical synthesis</a>"|"
The artificial execution of one or more <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical reaction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical reactions</span></a> in order to obtain one or more <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#product""><span title=""See entry on this page at § product"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">products</span></a>. In modern laboratory contexts, specific chemical syntheses are both reliable and reproducible.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemistry"" title=""Chemistry"">chemistry</a>"|"
The scientific discipline that studies <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_substance""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical substance"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical substances</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#compound""><span title=""See entry on this page at § compound"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">compounds</span></a>, and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecule"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molecules</span></a> composed of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atoms</span></a> of various <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#element""><span title=""See entry on this page at § element"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical elements</span></a>, as well as their <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_composition""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical composition"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">compositions</span></a>, structures, properties, behaviors, and the changes they undergo during <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical reaction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">reactions</span></a> with other substances.
"

"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cluster_chemistry"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Cluster chemistry"">cluster</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cohesion_(chemistry)"" title=""Cohesion (chemistry)"">cohesion</a>"|"
The tendency of similar particles or surfaces to cling to one another as a result of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#intermolecular_force""><span title=""See entry on this page at § intermolecular force"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">intermolecular forces</span></a>. Contrast <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#adhesion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § adhesion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">adhesion</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colligative_property"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Colligative property"">colligative property</a>"|"
Any property of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solution</span></a> that depends upon the ratio of the number of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solute""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solute"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solute</span></a> particles to the number of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solvent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solvent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solvent</span></a> particles in the solution, and not on the nature of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_species""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical species"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical species</span></a> present.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colloid"" title=""Colloid"">colloid</a>"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mixture""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mixture"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mixture</span></a> of evenly <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#dispersion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § dispersion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">dispersed</span></a> substances, such as many <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milk"" title=""Milk"">milks</a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Combustion"" title=""Combustion"">combustion</a>"|"
An <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#exothermic_process""><span title=""See entry on this page at § exothermic process"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">exothermic</span></a> reaction between an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#oxidant""><span title=""See entry on this page at § oxidant"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">oxidant</span></a> and a fuel that produces large amounts of heat and often light.

"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commission_on_Isotopic_Abundances_and_Atomic_Weights"" title=""Commission on Isotopic Abundances and Atomic Weights"">Commission on Isotopic Abundances and Atomic Weights</a> (CIAAW)"|"

<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compression_(physics)"" title=""Compression (physics)"">compression</a>"|"
An area in a longitudinal wave where the particles are closer and pushed in.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_compound"" title=""Chemical compound"">compound</a>"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_substance""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical substance"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">substance</span></a> that is made up of two or more <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemically bonded</span></a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#element""><span title=""See entry on this page at § element"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">elements</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concentration"" title=""Concentration"">concentration</a>"|"
The abundance of a constituent of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mixture""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mixture"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mixture</span></a> divided by the total <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#volume""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volume"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volume</span></a> of the mixture. Several different definitions of concentration are widely used in chemistry, including <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mass_concentration""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mass concentration"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mass concentration</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#volume_concentration""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volume concentration"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volume concentration</span></a>, and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molar_concentration""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molar concentration"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molar concentration</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Condensation"" title=""Condensation"">condensation</a>"|"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#phase_transition""><span title=""See entry on this page at § phase transition"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">phase transition</span></a> of a substance from a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#gas""><span title=""See entry on this page at § gas"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gas</span></a> to a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquid</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Condosity"" title=""Condosity"">condosity</a>"|"
A comparative measurement of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrical_conductivity"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Electrical conductivity"">electrical conductivity</a> of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solution</span></a> defined as the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molar_concentration""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molar concentration"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molar concentration</span></a> of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sodium_chloride"" title=""Sodium chloride"">sodium chloride</a> (NaCl) solution that has the same specific electrical conductance as the solution under test. It is typically expressed in units of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">moles</span></a> per <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#litre""><span title=""See entry on this page at § litre"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">litre</span></a> (or per some other unit of volume).
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrical_conductor"" title=""Electrical conductor"">conductor</a>"|"
Any object or material that allows the flow of an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electric_current""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electric current"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electric current</span></a> in one or more directions. Contrast <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#insulator""><span title=""See entry on this page at § insulator"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">insulator</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conformation_(chemistry)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Conformation (chemistry)"">conformation</a>"|"
The spatial arrangement of atoms affording distinction between <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#stereoisomer""><span title=""See entry on this page at § stereoisomer"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">stereoisomers</span></a> which can be interconverted by rotations about formally <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#single_bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § single bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">single bonds</span></a>.
"

"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coordination_complex"" title=""Coordination complex"">coordination complex</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corrosion"" title=""Corrosion"">corrosion</a>"|"
An irreversible interfacial <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical reaction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical reaction</span></a> of a material with its environment which results in consumption of the material or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#dissolution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § dissolution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">dissolution</span></a> into the material of an external component of the environment.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coulomb"" title=""Coulomb"">coulomb</a>"|"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#sI""><span title=""See entry on this page at § SI"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">SI</span></a> unit of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electric_charge""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electric charge"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electric charge</span></a> (symbol: <i>C</i>), defined as the charge transported by a constant <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electric_current""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electric current"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">current</span></a> of one <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ampere"" title=""Ampere"">ampere</a> in one <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second"" title=""Second"">second</a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Covalent_bond"" title=""Covalent bond"">covalent bond</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>molecular bond</b>.</span></p>
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bond</span></a> that involves the sharing of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron_pair""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron pair"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electron pairs</span></a> between <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atoms</span></a>. The stable balance of attractive and repulsive forces that occurs between atoms when they share electrons is known as <i>covalent bonding</i>.
<div class=""thumb tright""><div class=""thumbinner"" style=""width:222px;""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Covalent_bond_hydrogen.svg"" class=""image""><img alt="""" src=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Covalent_bond_hydrogen.svg/220px-Covalent_bond_hydrogen.svg.png"" decoding=""async"" width=""220"" height=""94"" class=""thumbimage"" srcset=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Covalent_bond_hydrogen.svg/330px-Covalent_bond_hydrogen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Covalent_bond_hydrogen.svg/440px-Covalent_bond_hydrogen.svg.png 2x"" data-file-width=""700"" data-file-height=""300"" /></a>  <div class=""thumbcaption""><div class=""magnify""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Covalent_bond_hydrogen.svg"" class=""internal"" title=""Enlarge""></a></div>The diatomic hydrogen molecule, H<sub>2</sub> (right), is formed by a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#covalent_bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § covalent bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">covalent bond</span></a> when two single hydrogen atoms share two electrons</div></div></div>"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Critical_point_(thermodynamics)"" title=""Critical point (thermodynamics)"">critical point</a>"|"
The end point of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#phase""><span title=""See entry on this page at § phase"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">phase</span></a> equilibrium curve or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#pressure""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pressure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pressure</span></a>-<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#temperature""><span title=""See entry on this page at § temperature"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">temperature</span></a> curve at which conditions are such that phase boundaries vanish and a substance's different phases, such as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquid</span></a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#vapor""><span title=""See entry on this page at § vapor"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">vapor</span></a>, can coexist. The critical point is defined by the intersection of a critical temperature, <i>T<sub>c</sub></i>, and a critical pressure, <i>p<sub>c</sub></i>; above this temperature and pressure, all distinction between phases disappears and the substance becomes a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#supercritical_fluid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § supercritical fluid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">supercritical fluid</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crystal"" title=""Crystal"">crystal</a>"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solid</span></a> whose constituent particles (such as atoms, ions, or molecules) are arranged in an orderly <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Periodic_function"" title=""Periodic function"">periodic</a> microscopic structure, forming a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#lattice""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lattice"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lattice</span></a> that extends in all directions. Such materials are often described as <i>crystalline</i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crystallography"" title=""Crystallography"">crystallography</a>"|"
The branch of chemistry concerned with determining the arrangement of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atoms</span></a> within <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#crystal""><span title=""See entry on this page at § crystal"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">crystalline</span></a> solids.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuvette"" title=""Cuvette"">cuvette</a>"|"
A type of glassware used in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#spectroscopy""><span title=""See entry on this page at § spectroscopy"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">spectroscopic</span></a> experiments. It is usually made of plastic, glass, or quartz and should be as clean and clear as possible."
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D-block"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""D-block"">d-block</a>"|"

"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dalton%27s_law"" title=""Dalton&#39;s law"">Dalton's law of partial pressures</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DI_water"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""DI water"">deionization</a>"|"
The removal of ions, and in water's case, mineral ions such as sodium, iron, and calcium.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deliquescence"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Deliquescence"">deliquescence</a>"|"
A substance's affinity for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water"" title=""Water"">water</a>, often characterized as its tendency to absorb moisture from the atmosphere to form <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#aqueous_solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § aqueous solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">aqueous solutions</span></a>. Most strongly deliquescent substances are <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#salt""><span title=""See entry on this page at § salt"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">salts</span></a>, such as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calcium_chloride"" title=""Calcium chloride"">calcium chloride</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Potassium_carbonate"" title=""Potassium carbonate"">potassium carbonate</a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delocalized_electron"" title=""Delocalized electron"">delocalized electron</a>"|"
Any <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electron</span></a> in a molecule, ion, or solid <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#metal""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metal"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">metal</span></a> that is not associated with an individual atom or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#covalent_bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § covalent bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">covalent bond</span></a>. The term may refer to electrons involved in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#resonance""><span title=""See entry on this page at § resonance"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">resonance</span></a> in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#conjugated_system""><span title=""See entry on this page at § conjugated system"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">conjugated systems</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#aromaticity""><span title=""See entry on this page at § aromaticity"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">aromatic</span></a> compounds; to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_electron_model"" title=""Free electron model"">free electrons</a> which facilitate <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrical_conductivity"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Electrical conductivity"">electrical conductivity</a>; or to electrons within delocalized <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecular_orbital""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecular orbital"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molecular orbitals</span></a> encompassing several adjacent atoms.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Density"" title=""Density"">density</a>"|"
An <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#intensive_property""><span title=""See entry on this page at § intensive property"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">intensive property</span></a> of a substance defined as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mass""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mass"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mass</span></a> per unit <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#volume""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volume"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volume</span></a> and expressed by the equation <i>d = m/V</i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denticity"" title=""Denticity"">denticity</a>"|"
The number of donor groups in a single <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ligand""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ligand"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ligand</span></a> that bind to a central atom in a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#coordination_complex""><span title=""See entry on this page at § coordination complex"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">coordination complex</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dependent_and_independent_variables"" title=""Dependent and independent variables"">dependent variable</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deposition_(chemistry)"" title=""Deposition (chemistry)"">deposition</a>"|"
The settling of particles within a solution or mixture.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dewar_flask"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Dewar flask"">Dewar flask</a>"|"
See <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#vacuum_flask""><span title=""See entry on this page at § vacuum flask"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">vacuum flask</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diatomic"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Diatomic"">diatomic</a>"|"
Composed of two atoms, of the same or different elements. Contrast <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#monatomic""><span title=""See entry on this page at § monatomic"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">monatomic</span></a></i> and <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#polyatomic""><span title=""See entry on this page at § polyatomic"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">polyatomic</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diatomic_molecule"" title=""Diatomic molecule"">diatomic molecule</a>"|"
Any <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecule"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molecule</span></a> composed of only two <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atoms</span></a>, of the same or different <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#element""><span title=""See entry on this page at § element"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">elements</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diffusion"" title=""Diffusion"">diffusion</a>"|"
The net movement of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atoms</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecule"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molecules</span></a> from a region of higher concentration to a region of lower concentration. Diffusion is driven by a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gradient"" title=""Gradient"">gradient</a> in chemical potential of the diffusing species and depends on the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Random_walk"" title=""Random walk"">random walk</a> of particles; hence it results in mixing or mass transport without required directed bulk motion.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dimer_(chemistry)"" title=""Dimer (chemistry)"">dimer</a>"|"
An <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#oligomer""><span title=""See entry on this page at § oligomer"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">oligomer</span></a> consisting of two <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#monomer""><span title=""See entry on this page at § monomer"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">monomers</span></a> joined by chemical bonds that may variably be strong or weak, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#covalent_bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § covalent bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">covalent</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#intermolecular_force""><span title=""See entry on this page at § intermolecular force"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">intermolecular</span></a>. A <i>homodimer</i> consists of two identical molecules; a <i>heterodimer</i> consists of two different molecules.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dipolar_bond"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Dipolar bond"">dipolar bond</a>"|"

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dipole"" title=""Dipole"">dipole</a>"|"
The electric or magnetic separation of charge.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bond_dipole_moment"" title=""Bond dipole moment"">dipole moment</a>"|"
The polarity of a polar covalent bond.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dispersion_(chemistry)"" title=""Dispersion (chemistry)"">dispersion</a>"|"
A system in which particles of one material are distributed within a continuous <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#phase""><span title=""See entry on this page at § phase"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">phase</span></a> of another material; the two phases may be in the same or different <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#state_of_matter""><span title=""See entry on this page at § state of matter"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">states of matter</span></a>. Dispersions of particles sufficiently large for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sedimentation"" title=""Sedimentation"">sedimentation</a> are called <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#suspension""><span title=""See entry on this page at § suspension"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">suspensions</span></a>, while those of smaller particles are called <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#colloid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § colloid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">colloids</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solutions</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dissociation_(chemistry)"" title=""Dissociation (chemistry)"">dissociation</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solvation"" title=""Solvation"">dissolution</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>solvation</b>.</span></p>
The interaction of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solvent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solvent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solvent</span></a> with the molecules or ions of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solute""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solute"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solute</span></a>, involving bond formation, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#hydrogen_bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hydrogen bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hydrogen bonding</span></a>, and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#van_der_Waals_force""><span title=""See entry on this page at § van der Waals force"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">van der Waals forces</span></a>.
<div class=""thumb tright""><div class=""thumbinner"" style=""width:222px;""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Na%2BH2O.svg"" class=""image""><img alt="""" src=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Na%2BH2O.svg/220px-Na%2BH2O.svg.png"" decoding=""async"" width=""220"" height=""220"" class=""thumbimage"" srcset=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Na%2BH2O.svg/330px-Na%2BH2O.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Na%2BH2O.svg/440px-Na%2BH2O.svg.png 2x"" data-file-width=""512"" data-file-height=""512"" /></a>  <div class=""thumbcaption""><div class=""magnify""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Na%2BH2O.svg"" class=""internal"" title=""Enlarge""></a></div>A sodium ion (Na<sup>+</sup>) forms a solvation complex with water molecules when <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#dissolution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § dissolution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">dissolved</span></a> in an aqueous solution</div></div></div>"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distillation"" title=""Distillation"">distillation</a>"|"
The process of separating the component substances of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquid</span></a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mixture""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mixture"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mixture</span></a> by exploiting differences in the relative <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#volatility""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volatility"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volatility</span></a> of the mixture's components through selective <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#boiling""><span title=""See entry on this page at § boiling"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">boiling</span></a> and subsequent <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#condensation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § condensation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">condensation</span></a>. The apparatus used to distill a substance is called a <i>still</i>, and the re-condensed substance yielded by the process is called the <i>distillate</i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double_bond"" title=""Double bond"">double bond</a>"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bond</span></a> involving the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#covalent_bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § covalent bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">covalent</span></a> sharing of two <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron_pair""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron pair"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pairs of electrons</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salt_metathesis_reaction"" title=""Salt metathesis reaction"">double-replacement reaction</a>"|"

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ductility"" title=""Ductility"">ductility</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>malleability</b>.</span></p>
A measure of a material's ability to undergo significant plastic deformation before rupturing, typically expressed as percent elongation or percent area reduction from a tensile test and popularly characterized by the material's ability to be stretched into a wire."
"earth metal"|"
See <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#alkaline_earth_metal""><span title=""See entry on this page at § alkaline earth metal"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">alkaline earth metal</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electric_charge"" title=""Electric charge"">electric charge</a>"|"
A measured property (<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#coulomb""><span title=""See entry on this page at § coulomb"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">coulombs</span></a>) that determines <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromagnetic_interaction"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Electromagnetic interaction"">electromagnetic interaction</a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrolyte"" title=""Electrolyte"">electrolyte</a>"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solution</span></a> that conducts a certain amount of electric current and can be split categorically into weak and strong electrolytes.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrochemical_cell"" title=""Electrochemical cell"">electrochemical cell</a>"|"
Using a chemical reaction's current, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electromotive_force""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electromotive force"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electromotive force</span></a> is made.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromagnetic_radiation"" title=""Electromagnetic radiation"">electromagnetic radiation</a>"|"
A type of wave that can go through vacuums as well as material and is classified as a self-propagating wave.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromagnetic_spectrum"" title=""Electromagnetic spectrum"">electromagnetic spectrum</a>"|"

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromagnetism"" title=""Electromagnetism"">electromagnetism</a>"|"
Fields with an electric charge and electrical properties that change the way that particles move and interact.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromotive_force"" title=""Electromotive force"">electromotive force</a> (emf)"|"

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electron"" title=""Electron"">electron</a>"|"
A type of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#subatomic_particle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § subatomic particle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">subatomic particle</span></a> with a net charge that is negative.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electron_configuration"" title=""Electron configuration"">electron configuration</a>"|"
The distribution of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electrons</span></a> of an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atom</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecule"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molecule</span></a> within <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atomic_orbital""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atomic orbital"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atomic</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecular_orbital""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecular orbital"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molecular orbitals</span></a>. An extensive system of notation is used to concisely and uniquely display information about the electron configuration of each atomic species. Knowledge of the specific arrangements of electrons in different atoms is useful for understanding <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical bonds</span></a> and the organization of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#periodic_table""><span title=""See entry on this page at § periodic table"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">periodic table of the elements</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electron_deficiency"" title=""Electron deficiency"">electron deficiency</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
