<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_number"" title=""Mass number"">mass number</a> (A)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>atomic mass number</b> or <b>nucleon number</b>.</span></p>
The total number of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#proton""><span title=""See entry on this page at § proton"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">protons</span></a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#neutron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § neutron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">neutrons</span></a> (together known as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#nucleon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § nucleon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">nucleons</span></a>) within the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#nucleus""><span title=""See entry on this page at § nucleus"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">nucleus</span></a> of an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atom</span></a>. It determines the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atomic_mass""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atomic mass"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atomic mass</span></a> of the atom. Mass number varies between different <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#isotope""><span title=""See entry on this page at § isotope"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">isotopes</span></a> of the same chemical element, and is often included either after the element's name (as in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon-12"" title=""Carbon-12"">carbon-12</a>) or as a superscript to the left of the element's symbol (as in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon-12"" title=""Carbon-12""><sup>12</sup>C</a>) to identify a specific isotope.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_spectrometry"" title=""Mass spectrometry"">mass spectrometry</a> (MS)"|"
An analytical technique that measures the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass-to-charge_ratio"" title=""Mass-to-charge ratio"">mass-to-charge ratio</a> of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ions</span></a> in a chemical sample by bombarding the sample with electrons to the point of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ionization""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ionization"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ionization</span></a> and then separating the charged fragments by subjecting them to an electric or magnetic field, typically in order to determine the elemental or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#isotopic_signature""><span title=""See entry on this page at § isotopic signature"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">isotopic signatures</span></a> of an unknown substance, the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mass""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mass"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">masses</span></a> of its constituent particles, and/or the identities or structures of the molecules within it. The results are presented as a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_spectrum"" title=""Mass spectrum"">mass spectrum</a>, a plot of the intensity of ion signals as a function of the mass-to-charge ratio.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matter"" title=""Matter"">matter</a>"|"
Any substance that has <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mass""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mass"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mass</span></a> and takes up space by having <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#volume""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volume"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volume</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metal"" title=""Metal"">metal</a>"|"
Any chemical element which is a good <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#conductor""><span title=""See entry on this page at § conductor"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">conductor</span></a> of both <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electricity""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electricity"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electricity</span></a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#heat""><span title=""See entry on this page at § heat"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">heat</span></a> and which readily forms <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#cation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cations</span></a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ionic_bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ionic bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ionic bonds</span></a> with <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#non-metal""><span title=""See entry on this page at § non-metal"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">non-metals</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melting"" title=""Melting"">melting</a>"|"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#phase_transition""><span title=""See entry on this page at § phase transition"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">phase transition</span></a> of a substance from a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solid</span></a> to a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquid</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melting_point"" title=""Melting point"">melting point</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>liquefaction point</b>.</span></p>
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#temperature""><span title=""See entry on this page at § temperature"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">temperature</span></a> at which a substance changes <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#state_of_matter""><span title=""See entry on this page at § state of matter"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">state</span></a> from a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solid</span></a> to a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquid</span></a>. It depends on <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#pressure""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pressure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pressure</span></a> and is usually specified for a given substance under <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#standard_temperature_and_pressure""><span title=""See entry on this page at § standard temperature and pressure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">standard conditions</span></a>. The melting point of a substance is identical to its <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#freezing_point""><span title=""See entry on this page at § freezing point"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">freezing point</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metalloid"" title=""Metalloid"">metalloid</a>"|"
A chemical element or substance possessing properties of both <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#metal""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metal"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">metals</span></a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#non-metal""><span title=""See entry on this page at § non-metal"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">non-metals</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Methylene_blue"" title=""Methylene blue"">methylene blue</a>"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heterocyclic_ring"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Heterocyclic ring"">heterocyclic</a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#aromaticity""><span title=""See entry on this page at § aromaticity"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">aromatic</span></a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#compound""><span title=""See entry on this page at § compound"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">compound</span></a> with the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecular_formula""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecular formula"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molecular formula</span></a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#carbon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § carbon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">C</span></a><sub>16</sub><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#hydrogen""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hydrogen"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">H</span></a><sub>18</sub><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#nitrogen""><span title=""See entry on this page at § nitrogen"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">N</span></a><sub>3</sub><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sulfur"" title=""Sulfur"">S</a><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlorine"" title=""Chlorine"">Cl</a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microcentrifuge"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Microcentrifuge"">microcentrifuge tube</a>"|"
A small plastic, sealable container that is used to store small volumes of liquid, generally less than 2 milliliters.
<div class=""thumb tright""><div class=""thumbinner"" style=""width:222px;""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Coomassie_solution.jpg"" class=""image""><img alt="""" src=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Coomassie_solution.jpg/220px-Coomassie_solution.jpg"" decoding=""async"" width=""220"" height=""165"" class=""thumbimage"" srcset=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Coomassie_solution.jpg/330px-Coomassie_solution.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Coomassie_solution.jpg/440px-Coomassie_solution.jpg 2x"" data-file-width=""2288"" data-file-height=""1712"" /></a>  <div class=""thumbcaption""><div class=""magnify""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Coomassie_solution.jpg"" class=""internal"" title=""Enlarge""></a></div>A 1.7-milliliter <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#microcentrifuge_tube""><span title=""See entry on this page at § microcentrifuge tube"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">microcentrifuge tube</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#eppendorf_tube""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Eppendorf tube"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Eppendorf tube</span></a> containing <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coomassie_Blue"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Coomassie Blue"">Coomassie Blue</a> solution</div></div></div>"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mineral"" title=""Mineral"">mineral</a>"|"

"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miscibility"" title=""Miscibility"">miscibility</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mixture"" title=""Mixture"">mixture</a>"|"
A material made up of two or more different substances which are mixed physically but are not combined chemically (i.e. a chemical reaction has not taken place which has changed the molecules of the substances into new substances).
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moiety_(chemistry)"" title=""Moiety (chemistry)"">moiety</a>"|"
Any named characteristic group, branch, or other part of a large <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecule"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molecule</span></a> that may be identified within other kinds of molecules as well. <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#functional_group""><span title=""See entry on this page at § functional group"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Functional groups</span></a> are typically smaller and more generic than moieties, whereas <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#substituent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § substituent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">substituents</span></a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#side_chain""><span title=""See entry on this page at § side chain"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">side chains</span></a> may often be classified as moieties and vice versa.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molality"" title=""Molality"">molality</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>molal concentration</b>.</span></p>
A measure of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#concentration""><span title=""See entry on this page at § concentration"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">concentration</span></a> of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solute""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solute"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solute</span></a> in a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solution</span></a> in terms of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#amount_of_substance""><span title=""See entry on this page at § amount of substance"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">amount</span></a> of the solute per unit <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mass""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mass"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mass</span></a> of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solvent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solvent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solvent</span></a>. Molality is typically expressed in units of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">moles</span></a> per <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#kilogram""><span title=""See entry on this page at § kilogram"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">kilogram</span></a> (mol/kg); a solution with a concentration of exactly 1 mol/kg is sometimes said to be <i>1 molal</i>. Contrast <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molar_concentration""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molar concentration"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molarity</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molar_attenuation_coefficient"" title=""Molar attenuation coefficient"">molar attenuation coefficient</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molar_concentration"" title=""Molar concentration"">molar concentration</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>molarity</b>, <b>amount concentration</b>, or <b>substance concentration</b>.</span></p>
A measure of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#concentration""><span title=""See entry on this page at § concentration"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">concentration</span></a> of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_species""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical species"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical species</span></a>, especially of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solute""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solute"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solute</span></a> in a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solution</span></a>, in terms of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#amount_of_substance""><span title=""See entry on this page at § amount of substance"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">amount</span></a> of the species per unit <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#volume""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volume"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volume</span></a> of solution. Molarity is typically expressed in units of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">moles</span></a> per <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#litre""><span title=""See entry on this page at § litre"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">litre</span></a> (mol/L); a solution with a concentration of exactly 1 mol/L is commonly said to be <i>1 molar</i>, symbolized as <i>1 M</i>. Contrast <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molality""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molality"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molality</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molar_fraction"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Molar fraction"">molar fraction</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>mole fraction</b>.</span></p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molar_mass"" title=""Molar mass"">molar mass</a>"|"

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mole_(unit)"" title=""Mole (unit)"">mole</a> (mol)"|"
A unit (symbol: <i>mol</i>) that measures the amount of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_substance""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical substance"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">substance</span></a> in terms of the absolute number of particles or entities composing the substance. A single mole contains approximately <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#avogadro&#39;s_number""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Avogadro&#39;s number"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">6.022×10<sup>23</sup></span></a> particles or entities.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecular_formula"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Molecular formula"">molecular formula</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecular_orbital"" title=""Molecular orbital"">molecular orbital</a> (MO)"|"
Any region in which one or more <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electrons</span></a> may be found in a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecule"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molecule</span></a> (as opposed to that within <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atomic_orbital""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atomic orbital"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">an individual atom</span></a>).
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecular_orbital_diagram"" title=""Molecular orbital diagram"">molecular orbital diagram</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecule"" title=""Molecule"">molecule</a>"|"
A number of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atoms</span></a> that are chemically <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bonded</span></a> together and collectively electrically neutral.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monatomic"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Monatomic"">monatomic</a>"|"
Having only one <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atom</span></a>, as opposed to a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecule"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molecule</span></a> composed of more than one. Virtually all elements are monatomic in the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#gas""><span title=""See entry on this page at § gas"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gas</span></a> phase at sufficiently high temperatures. Contrast <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#diatomic""><span title=""See entry on this page at § diatomic"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">diatomic</span></a></i> and <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#polyatomic""><span title=""See entry on this page at § polyatomic"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">polyatomic</span></a></i>."
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_abundance"" title=""Natural abundance"">natural abundance</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"neat"|"
Conditions with a liquid reagent or gas performed with no added solvent or cosolvent.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neutron"" title=""Neutron"">neutron</a>"|"
A type of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#subatomic_particle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § subatomic particle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">subatomic particle</span></a> that is electrically neutral, having no net charge.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrogen"" title=""Nitrogen"">nitrogen</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleon"" title=""Nucleon"">nucleon</a>"|"
Either a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#proton""><span title=""See entry on this page at § proton"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">proton</span></a> or a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#neutron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § neutron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">neutron</span></a>, considered in its role as a component of an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#nucleus""><span title=""See entry on this page at § nucleus"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atomic nucleus</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleophile"" title=""Nucleophile"">nucleophile</a>"|"
Any atom or molecule which can donate an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron_pair""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron pair"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electron pair</span></a> to another atom or molecule. All molecules or ions with a free pair of electrons or at least one <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#pi_bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pi bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pi bond</span></a> can act as nucleophiles, by which they are attracted to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron_deficiency""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron deficiency"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electron-deficient</span></a> regions of other species; a chemical reaction involving a nucleophile donating an electron pair to an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electrophile""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electrophile"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electrophile</span></a> may be referred to as <i>nucleophilic attack</i>. Because they donate electrons, nucleophiles are <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#lewis_base""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Lewis base"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Lewis bases</span></a> by definition.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_nucleus"" title=""Atomic nucleus"">nucleus</a>"|"
The centre of an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atom</span></a>, made up of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#neutron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § neutron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">neutrons</span></a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#proton""><span title=""See entry on this page at § proton"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">protons</span></a> and possessing a net positive electric charge.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Noble_gas"" title=""Noble gas"">noble gas</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>inert gas</b>.</span></p>
Any of the six <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#non-metal""><span title=""See entry on this page at § non-metal"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">non-metallic</span></a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#element""><span title=""See entry on this page at § element"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">elements</span></a> of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#group""><span title=""See entry on this page at § group"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Group 18</span></a> of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#periodic_table""><span title=""See entry on this page at § periodic table"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">periodic table</span></a>: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helium"" title=""Helium"">helium</a> (He), <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neon"" title=""Neon"">neon</a> (Ne), <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Argon"" title=""Argon"">argon</a> (Ar), <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Krypton"" title=""Krypton"">krypton</a> (Kr), <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xenon"" title=""Xenon"">xenon</a> (Xe), and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radon"" title=""Radon"">radon</a> (Rn). All of the noble gases have outer <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron_shell""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron shell"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electron shells</span></a> that are completely filled in their naturally occurring states, giving them very low chemical reactivity.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-metal"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Non-metal"">non-metal</a>"|"
Any chemical element which is not a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#metal""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metal"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">metal</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Normality_(chemistry)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Normality (chemistry)"">normality</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_nucleus"" title=""Atomic nucleus"">nuclear</a>"|"
Of or pertaining to the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#nucleus""><span title=""See entry on this page at § nucleus"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atomic nucleus</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_chemistry"" title=""Nuclear chemistry"">nuclear chemistry</a>"|"
The branch of chemistry that studies the various processes and properties relevant to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#nucleus""><span title=""See entry on this page at § nucleus"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atomic nuclei</span></a>, including <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#radioactivity""><span title=""See entry on this page at § radioactivity"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">radioactivity</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_magnetic_resonance_spectroscopy"" title=""Nuclear magnetic resonance spectroscopy"">nuclear magnetic resonance spectroscopy</a>"|"
A technique that exploits the magnetic properties of certain nuclei, useful for identifying unknown compounds. Nuclear magnetic resonance is often abbreviated <i>NMR</i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_transmutation"" title=""Nuclear transmutation"">nuclear transmutation</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclide"" title=""Nuclide"">nuclide</a>"|"
A species of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atom</span></a> characterized by its <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mass_number""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mass number"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mass number</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atomic_number""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atomic number"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atomic number</span></a>, and nuclear energy state, provided that the mean life in that state is long enough to be observable.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Number_density"" title=""Number density"">number density</a>"|"
A measure of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#concentration""><span title=""See entry on this page at § concentration"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">concentration</span></a> of countable objects (atoms, molecules, etc.) in space, expressed as the number per unit <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#volume""><span title=""See entry on this page at § volume"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">volume</span></a>."
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Octet_rule"" title=""Octet rule"">octet rule</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>Lewis octet rule</b>.</span></p>
A classical rule for describing the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron_configuration""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron configuration"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electron configuration</span></a> of atoms in certain molecules: the maximum number of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron_pair""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron pair"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electron pairs</span></a> that can be accommodated in the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#valence_electron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § valence electron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">valence</span></a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron_shell""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron shell"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">shell</span></a> of an element in the first row of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#periodic_table""><span title=""See entry on this page at § periodic table"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">periodic table</span></a> is four (or eight total electrons). For elements in the second and subsequent rows, there are many exceptions to this rule.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olefin"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Olefin"">olefin</a>"|"
A trivial (non-<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#international_Union_of_Pure_and_Applied_Chemistry""><span title=""See entry on this page at § International Union of Pure and Applied Chemistry"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">IUPAC</span></a>) name for any <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#alkene""><span title=""See entry on this page at § alkene"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">alkene</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optical_activity"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Optical activity"">optical activity</a>"|"

<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"orbital"|"
Any region of an atom or molecule in which one or more <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electrons</span></a> can be found. The term may refer to either an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atomic_orbital""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atomic orbital"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atomic orbital</span></a> or a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecular_orbital""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecular orbital"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molecular orbital</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbital_hybridisation"" title=""Orbital hybridisation"">orbital hybridisation</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_reaction"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Order of reaction"">order of reaction</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organic_acid"" title=""Organic acid"">organic acid</a>"|"
Any <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#organic_compound""><span title=""See entry on this page at § organic compound"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">organic compound</span></a> with <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#acid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § acid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">acidic</span></a> properties. Contrast <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#organic_base""><span title=""See entry on this page at § organic base"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">organic base</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organic_base"" title=""Organic base"">organic base</a>"|"
Any <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#organic_compound""><span title=""See entry on this page at § organic compound"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">organic compound</span></a> with <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#base""><span title=""See entry on this page at § base"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">basic</span></a> properties. Contrast <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#organic_acid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § organic acid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">organic acid</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organic_compound"" title=""Organic compound"">organic compound</a>"|"
Any <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#compound""><span title=""See entry on this page at § compound"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical compound</span></a> that contains one or more <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#carbon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § carbon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">carbon</span></a> atoms. Contrast <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#inorganic_compound""><span title=""See entry on this page at § inorganic compound"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">inorganic compound</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organic_chemistry"" title=""Organic chemistry"">organic chemistry</a>"|"
The branch of chemistry concerned with the chemical properties and reactions of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#organic_compound""><span title=""See entry on this page at § organic compound"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">organic compounds</span></a>. Contrast <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#inorganic_chemistry""><span title=""See entry on this page at § inorganic chemistry"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">inorganic chemistry</span></a></i>.
"

"other metal"|"
Any of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#metal""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metal"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">metallic</span></a> elements in the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#p-block""><span title=""See entry on this page at § p-block"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">p-block</span></a>, which are characterized by having a combination of relatively low <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#melting_point""><span title=""See entry on this page at § melting point"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">melting points</span></a> (all less than 950 K) and relatively high <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electronegativity""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electronegativity"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electronegativity</span></a> values (all more than 1.6, revised Pauling).

"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxidation_state"" title=""Oxidation state"">oxidation state</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>oxidation number</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;The degree of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#oxidation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § oxidation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">oxidation</span></a> of an individual atom in a chemical compound, measured as the decrease in the number of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electrons</span></a> relative to the atom's naturally occurring elemental state.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;The hypothetical <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electric_charge""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electric charge"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electric charge</span></a> (positive, negative, or zero) that an atom would have if all bonds to atoms of different elements were 100% <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ionic_bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ionic bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ionic</span></a>, with no <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#covalent_bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § covalent bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">covalent</span></a> component.</dd>
"

"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxoacid"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Oxoacid"">oxoacid</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>oxyacid</b> or <b>oxacid</b>.</span></p>
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;Any <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#acid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § acid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">acid</span></a> having <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#oxygen""><span title=""See entry on this page at § oxygen"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">oxygen</span></a> in the acidic group.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;Any compound which contains oxygen, at least one other element, and at least one <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#hydrogen""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hydrogen"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hydrogen</span></a> atom bound to oxygen, and which produces a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#conjugate_base""><span title=""See entry on this page at § conjugate base"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">conjugate base</span></a> by the loss of positive hydrogen <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ions</span></a>.</dd>
"

"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paraffin_(disambiguation)"" class=""mw-redirect mw-disambig"" title=""Paraffin (disambiguation)"">paraffin</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A trivial (non-<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#international_Union_of_Pure_and_Applied_Chemistry""><span title=""See entry on this page at § International Union of Pure and Applied Chemistry"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">IUPAC</span></a>) name for any <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#alkane""><span title=""See entry on this page at § alkane"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">alkane</span></a>.</dd>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PH"" title=""PH"">pH</a>"|"
A logarithmic scale used to specify the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#acid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § acid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">acidity</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#base""><span title=""See entry on this page at § base"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">basicity</span></a> of an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#aqueous_solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § aqueous solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">aqueous solution</span></a>. The pH scale approximates the negative of the base-10 logarithm of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molar_concentration""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molar concentration"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molar concentration</span></a> of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#hydrogen""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hydrogen"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hydrogen</span></a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ions</span></a> in a solution. At <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#room_temperature""><span title=""See entry on this page at § room temperature"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">room temperature</span></a>, pure water is neutral (pH = 7); solutions with a pH less than 7 are acidic and those with a pH greater than 7 are basic.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phase_(matter)"" title=""Phase (matter)"">phase</a>"|"
A region of space throughout which all physical properties of a substance are essentially uniform, or a region of material that is chemically uniform, physically distinct, and often mechanically separable. The term <i>phase</i> may have several different uses in chemistry contexts; colloquially, it is often used interchangeably with <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#state_of_matter""><span title=""See entry on this page at § state of matter"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">state of matter</span></a>, but many distinct phases may exist within a single state of matter.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phase_transition"" title=""Phase transition"">phase transition</a>"|"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A transformation of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_substance""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical substance"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical substance</span></a> between <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solid</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquid</span></a>, and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#gas""><span title=""See entry on this page at § gas"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gaseous</span></a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#state_of_matter""><span title=""See entry on this page at § state of matter"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">states of matter</span></a> and, in rare cases, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#plasma""><span title=""See entry on this page at § plasma"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">plasma</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;The measurable values of the external conditions at which such a transformation occurs.</dd>
<div class=""thumb tright""><div class=""thumbinner"" style=""width:222px;""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Phase_change_-_en.svg"" class=""image""><img alt="""" src=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Phase_change_-_en.svg/220px-Phase_change_-_en.svg.png"" decoding=""async"" width=""220"" height=""234"" class=""thumbimage"" srcset=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Phase_change_-_en.svg/330px-Phase_change_-_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Phase_change_-_en.svg/440px-Phase_change_-_en.svg.png 2x"" data-file-width=""493"" data-file-height=""524"" /></a>  <div class=""thumbcaption""><div class=""magnify""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Phase_change_-_en.svg"" class=""internal"" title=""Enlarge""></a></div>This diagram shows the nomenclature commonly used for each of the different <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#phase_transition""><span title=""See entry on this page at § phase transition"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">phase transitions</span></a></div></div></div>"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phi_bond"" title=""Phi bond"">phi bond</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
