"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physical_chemistry"" title=""Physical chemistry"">physical chemistry</a>"|"
The branch of chemistry that studies chemical systems in terms of the principles, practices, and concepts of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physics"" title=""Physics"">physics</a>, such as motion, energy, force, time, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thermodynamics"" title=""Thermodynamics"">thermodynamics</a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_equilibrium""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical equilibrium"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical equilibrium</span></a>, and statistical mechanics, among others. In contrast to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_physics"" title=""Chemical physics"">chemical physics</a>, physical chemistry is predominantly (though not entirely) a macroscopic science that studies the physical and chemical interactions of bulk quantities of matter.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pi_bond"" title=""Pi bond"">pi bond</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pipette"" title=""Pipette"">pipette</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also spelled <b>pipet</b>.</span></p>
A laboratory tool commonly used in chemistry, biology, and medicine to transfer and dispense a precisely measured volume of liquid.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plasma_(physics)"" title=""Plasma (physics)"">plasma</a>"|"
One of the four fundamental <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#state_of_matter""><span title=""See entry on this page at § state of matter"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">states of matter</span></a>, in which very high-energy particles are partially or fully <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ionization""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ionization"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ionized</span></a> to the point that they display unique properties and behaviors unlike those of the other three states. Plasma does not exist freely on the Earth's surface under natural conditions.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Period_(periodic_table)"" title=""Period (periodic table)"">period</a>"|"
A horizontal row of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#periodic_table""><span title=""See entry on this page at § periodic table"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">periodic table of the elements</span></a> and the elements that share it. Contrast <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#group""><span title=""See entry on this page at § group"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">group</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Periodic_table_of_the_elements"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Periodic table of the elements"">periodic table of the elements</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also simply called the <b>periodic table</b>.</span></p>
A tabular arrangement of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#element""><span title=""See entry on this page at § element"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical elements</span></a> organized by their <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atomic_number""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atomic number"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atomic number</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron_configuration""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron configuration"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electron configuration</span></a>, and other chemical properties, whose adopted structure shows <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Periodic_trends"" title=""Periodic trends"">periodic trends</a> and is used by chemists to derive relationships between various elements as well as predict the properties and behaviors of undiscovered or newly synthesized elements. The first periodic table of the elements was published by Russian chemist <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dmitri_Mendeleev"" title=""Dmitri Mendeleev"">Dmitri Mendeleev</a> in 1869.
<div class=""thumb tright""><div class=""thumbinner"" style=""width:222px;""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Simple_Periodic_Table_Chart-en.svg"" class=""image""><img alt="""" src=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Simple_Periodic_Table_Chart-en.svg/220px-Simple_Periodic_Table_Chart-en.svg.png"" decoding=""async"" width=""220"" height=""116"" class=""thumbimage"" srcset=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Simple_Periodic_Table_Chart-en.svg/330px-Simple_Periodic_Table_Chart-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Simple_Periodic_Table_Chart-en.svg/440px-Simple_Periodic_Table_Chart-en.svg.png 2x"" data-file-width=""1205"" data-file-height=""638"" /></a>  <div class=""thumbcaption""><div class=""magnify""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Simple_Periodic_Table_Chart-en.svg"" class=""internal"" title=""Enlarge""></a></div>The modern <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#periodic_table""><span title=""See entry on this page at § periodic table"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">periodic table of the elements</span></a>. The horizontal rows are called <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#period""><span title=""See entry on this page at § period"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">periods</span></a> and the vertical columns are called <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#group""><span title=""See entry on this page at § group"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">groups</span></a> or families.</div></div></div>"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_polarity"" title=""Chemical polarity"">polarity</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Potential_energy"" title=""Potential energy"">potential energy</a>"|"
The stored energy in a body or in a system due to its position in a force field or due to its configuration.
"
"precipitate"|"
The formation of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solid</span></a> in a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solution</span></a> or inside another solid during a chemical reaction or by diffusion in a solid.
"
"precision"|"
How close the results of multiple experimental trials or observations are to each other. Compare <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#accuracy""><span title=""See entry on this page at § accuracy"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">accuracy</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pressure"" title=""Pressure"">pressure</a>"|"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Force"" title=""Force"">force</a> applied perpendicular to the surface of an object per unit <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Area"" title=""Area"">area</a>. The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#sI""><span title=""See entry on this page at § SI"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">SI</span></a> unit for pressure is the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#pascal""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pascal"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pascal</span></a> (Pa), though many other units of pressure are also commonly used in chemistry.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photon"" title=""Photon"">photon</a>"|"
A carrier of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electromagnetic_radiation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electromagnetic radiation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electromagnetic radiation</span></a> of all wavelengths (such as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamma_ray"" title=""Gamma ray"">gamma rays</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio_wave"" title=""Radio wave"">radio waves</a>).
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polyatomic"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Polyatomic"">polyatomic</a>"|"
Composed of two or more atoms, of the same or different elements. Contrast <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#monatomic""><span title=""See entry on this page at § monatomic"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">monatomic</span></a></i> and <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#diatomic""><span title=""See entry on this page at § diatomic"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">diatomic</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polyatomic_ion"" title=""Polyatomic ion"">polyatomic ion</a>"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecule"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molecule</span></a> composed of two or more <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#covalent_bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § covalent bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">covalently bonded</span></a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atoms</span></a> which collectively bear a net <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electric_charge""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electric charge"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electric charge</span></a> and therefore act as an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ion</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protective_group"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Protective group"">protective group</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proton"" title=""Proton"">proton</a>"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#subatomic_particle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § subatomic particle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">subatomic particle</span></a> with a positive electric charge that is found in the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#nucleus""><span title=""See entry on this page at § nucleus"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">nucleus</span></a> of an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atom</span></a>. Often denoted with the symbol <i>H<sup>+</sup></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protonation"" title=""Protonation"">protonation</a>"|"
The addition of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#proton""><span title=""See entry on this page at § proton"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">proton</span></a> (H<sup>+</sup>) to an atom, molecule, or ion.
"
"pure substance"|"
See <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_substance""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical substance"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical substance</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pyrolysis"" title=""Pyrolysis"">pyrolysis</a>"|"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thermal_decomposition"" title=""Thermal decomposition"">thermal decomposition</a> of materials at elevated temperatures in an inert atmosphere such as a vacuum gas."
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_mechanics"" title=""Quantum mechanics"">quantum mechanics</a>"|"
The study of how atoms, molecules, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#subatomic_particle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § subatomic particle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">subatomic particles</span></a>, etc. behave and are structured.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quark"" title=""Quark"">quark</a>"|"
An elementary particle and a fundamental constituent of matter.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum"" title=""Quantum"">quantum</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">pl. <b>quanta</b></span></p>"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Racemate"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Racemate"">racemate</a>"|"
An equimolar <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mixture""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mixture"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mixture</span></a> of a pair of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#enantiomer""><span title=""See entry on this page at § enantiomer"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">enantiomers</span></a> which does not exhibit <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#optical_activity""><span title=""See entry on this page at § optical activity"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">optical activity</span></a>. The chemical name or formula of a racemate is distinguished from those of the enantiomers by the prefix <i>(±)-</i> or by the symbols <i>RS</i> and <i>SR</i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radiation"" title=""Radiation"">radiation</a>"|"
Energy released in the form of waves or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#subatomic_particle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § subatomic particle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">subatomic particles</span></a> when there is a change from high-energy to low-energy states.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radical_(chemistry)"" title=""Radical (chemistry)"">radical</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>free radical</b>.</span></p>
Any atom, molecule, or ion that has at least one <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#unpaired_electron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § unpaired electron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">unpaired</span></a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#valence_electron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § valence electron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">valence electron</span></a>. With few exceptions, such unpaired electrons make radicals highly chemically reactive, and therefore organic radicals are usually short-lived.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radioactive_decay"" title=""Radioactive decay"">radioactive decay</a>"|"
The process of an unstable atomic nucleus losing energy by emitting radiation.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raoult%27s_law"" title=""Raoult&#39;s law"">Raoult's law</a>"|"
A law of thermodynamics which states that the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#partial_pressure""><span title=""See entry on this page at § partial pressure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">partial pressure</span></a> of each <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#gas""><span title=""See entry on this page at § gas"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gaseous</span></a> component of an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ideal_solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ideal solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ideal mixture</span></a> of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquids</span></a> is equal to the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#vapor_pressure""><span title=""See entry on this page at § vapor pressure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">vapor pressure</span></a> of the pure component multiplied by its <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molar_fraction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molar fraction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molar fraction</span></a> in the mixture.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rare-earth_metal"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Rare-earth metal"">rare-earth metal</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rate_equation"" title=""Rate equation"">rate equation</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>rate law</b>.</span></p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reactant"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Reactant"">reactant</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Sometimes used interchangeably with <b><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#reagent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § reagent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">reagent</span></a></b>.</span></p>
Any substance that is consumed in the course of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical reaction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical reaction</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reaction_mechanism"" title=""Reaction mechanism"">reaction mechanism</a>"|"
The step-by-step sequence of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#elementary_reaction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § elementary reaction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">elementary reactions</span></a> by which a larger <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical reaction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical reaction</span></a> or overall change occurs. A complete mechanism must describe and explain which <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bonds</span></a> are broken and which are formed (and in what order), as well as all <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#reactant""><span title=""See entry on this page at § reactant"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">reactants</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#product""><span title=""See entry on this page at § product"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">products</span></a>, and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#catalyst""><span title=""See entry on this page at § catalyst"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">catalysts</span></a> involved; the amounts of each; all <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#reactive_intermediate""><span title=""See entry on this page at § reactive intermediate"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">intermediates</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#activated_complex""><span title=""See entry on this page at § activated complex"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">activated complexes</span></a>, and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#transition_state""><span title=""See entry on this page at § transition state"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">transition states</span></a>; and the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#stereochemistry""><span title=""See entry on this page at § stereochemistry"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">stereochemistry</span></a> of each chemical species. Because the detailed processes of a complex reaction are not observable in most cases, a reaction mechanism is often a theoretical conjecture based on thermodynamic feasibility and what little support can be gained from experiment.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reaction_rate"" title=""Reaction rate"">reaction rate</a>"|"
The speed at which <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#reactant""><span title=""See entry on this page at § reactant"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">reactants</span></a> are converted into <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#product""><span title=""See entry on this page at § product"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">products</span></a> in a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical reaction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical reaction</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reaction_rate_constant"" title=""Reaction rate constant"">reaction rate constant</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reactive_intermediate"" title=""Reactive intermediate"">reactive intermediate</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also simply called an <b>intermediate</b>.</span></p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reactivity_(chemistry)"" title=""Reactivity (chemistry)"">reactivity</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reactivity_series"" title=""Reactivity series"">reactivity series</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>activity series</b>.</span></p>
An empirical, calculated, and structurally analytical progression of a series of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#metal""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metal"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">metals</span></a>, arranged by their general <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#reactivity""><span title=""See entry on this page at § reactivity"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">reactivity</span></a> from highest to lowest and used to summarize information about their reactions with <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#acid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § acid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">acids</span></a> and water and the methods used to extract them from ores.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reagent"" title=""Reagent"">reagent</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also another name for a <b><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#reactant""><span title=""See entry on this page at § reactant"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">reactant</span></a></b>.</span></p>
A test substance that is added to a system in order to bring about a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical reaction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical reaction</span></a>, or to see whether a reaction occurs.
"

"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Retort"" title=""Retort"">retort</a>"|"
A laboratory apparatus used for the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#distillation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § distillation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">distillation</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#dry_distillation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § dry distillation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">dry distillation</span></a> of chemical substances, traditionally consisting of a spherical vessel with a long, downward-pointing neck that conducts the condensed vapors produced by distillation into a separate collection vessel.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Round-bottom_flask"" title=""Round-bottom flask"">round-bottom flask</a>"|"

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S-block"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""S-block"">s-block</a>"|"
The collective name for the elements in Groups 1 and 2 of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#periodic_table""><span title=""See entry on this page at § periodic table"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">periodic table</span></a> (the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#alkali_metal""><span title=""See entry on this page at § alkali metal"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">alkali</span></a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#alkaline_metal""><span title=""See entry on this page at § alkaline metal"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">alkaline metals</span></a>), as well as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydrogen"" title=""Hydrogen"">hydrogen</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helium"" title=""Helium"">helium</a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salt_(chemistry)"" title=""Salt (chemistry)"">salt</a>"|"
Any <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#ionic_compound""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ionic compound"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ionic compound</span></a> composed of one or more <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#anion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § anion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">anions</span></a> and one or more <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#cation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cations</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salt_bridge"" title=""Salt bridge"">salt bridge</a>"|"
A device used to connect reduction with oxidation half-cells in an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electrochemical_cell""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electrochemical cell"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electrochemical cell</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saline_(medicine)"" title=""Saline (medicine)"">saline solution</a>"|"
A common term for a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solution</span></a> of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sodium_chloride"" title=""Sodium chloride"">sodium chloride</a> (NaCl) dissolved in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water"" title=""Water"">water</a> (H<sub>2</sub>O).
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schr%C3%B6dinger_equation"" title=""Schrödinger equation"">Schrödinger equation</a>"|"
A quantum state equation which represents the behaviour of an election around an atom.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rate_equation#Second_order_reactions"" title=""Rate equation"">second-order reaction</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semiconductor"" title=""Semiconductor"">semiconductor</a>"|"
An electrically conductive solid whose degree of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrical_conductivity"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Electrical conductivity"">conductivity</a> lies somewhere between that of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#conductor""><span title=""See entry on this page at § conductor"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">conductor</span></a> and that of an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#insulator""><span title=""See entry on this page at § insulator"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">insulator</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serial_dilution"" title=""Serial dilution"">serial dilution</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Side_chain"" title=""Side chain"">side chain</a>"|"
A chemical <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#substituent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § substituent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">substituent group</span></a> that is attached to the core part or ""<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backbone_chain"" title=""Backbone chain"">backbone</a>"" of a larger <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#molecule""><span title=""See entry on this page at § molecule"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">molecule</span></a>, especially an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oligomer"" title=""Oligomer"">oligomeric</a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polymer"" title=""Polymer"">polymeric</a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#hydrocarbon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hydrocarbon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hydrocarbon</span></a> chain that branches off of the longer primary chain of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macromolecule"" title=""Macromolecule"">macromolecule</a>, as used in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#biochemistry""><span title=""See entry on this page at § biochemistry"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">biochemistry</span></a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#organic_chemistry""><span title=""See entry on this page at § organic chemistry"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">organic chemistry</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multiple_bond"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Multiple bond"">single bond</a>"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bond</span></a> that involves the sharing of one <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron_pair""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron pair"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pair of electrons</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Skeletal_formula"" title=""Skeletal formula"">skeletal formula</a>"|"

<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sol_(colloid)"" title=""Sol (colloid)"">sol</a>"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#suspension""><span title=""See entry on this page at § suspension"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">suspension</span></a> of solid particles in a liquid. Artificial examples include <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sol-gel"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Sol-gel"">sol-gels</a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solid"" title=""Solid"">solid</a>"|"
One of the four fundamental <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#state_of_matter""><span title=""See entry on this page at § state of matter"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">states of matter</span></a>, characterized by relatively low-energy particles packed closely together in rigid structures with definite shape and volume. See <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#young&#39;s_modulus""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Young&#39;s modulus"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Young's modulus</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solubility"" title=""Solubility"">solubility</a>"|"
The property of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solid</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquid</span></a>, or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#gas""><span title=""See entry on this page at § gas"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gaseous</span></a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solute""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solute"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solute</span></a> to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#dissolution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § dissolution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">dissolve</span></a> in a solid, liquid, or gaseous <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solvent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solvent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solvent</span></a>. It is typically expressed as the proportion of solute dissolved in the solvent in a saturated solution.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solution"" title=""Solution"">solute</a>"|"
The part of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solution</span></a> that is dissolved into the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solvent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solvent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solvent</span></a>. For example, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sodium_chloride"" title=""Sodium chloride"">sodium chloride</a> (NaCl) is the solute in a solution of saline water.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solution"" title=""Solution"">solution</a>"|"
A homogeneous <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mixture""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mixture"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mixture</span></a> made up of multiple substances generally referred to as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solute""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solute"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solutes</span></a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solvent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solvent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solvents</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solvated_electron"" title=""Solvated electron"">solvated electron</a>"|"

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solvent"" title=""Solvent"">solvent</a>"|"
The part of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solution</span></a> that dissolves the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solute""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solute"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solute</span></a>. For example, water (H<sub>2</sub>O) is the solvent in a solution of saline water.
"

"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spectroscopy"" title=""Spectroscopy"">spectroscopy</a>"|"
The study of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#radiation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § radiation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">radiation</span></a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#matter""><span title=""See entry on this page at § matter"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">matter</span></a>, such as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#x-ray""><span title=""See entry on this page at § X-ray"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">X-ray</span></a> absorption and emission spectroscopy.

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_conditions_of_temperature_and_pressure"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Standard conditions of temperature and pressure"">standard conditions of temperature and pressure</a> (STP)"|"
A standardisation of ambient <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#temperature""><span title=""See entry on this page at § temperature"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">temperature</span></a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#pressure""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pressure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pressure</span></a> used in order to easily compare experimental results. Standard temperature is 25 degrees Celsius (°C) and standard pressure is 100.000 kilopascals (kPa). Standard conditions are often denoted with the abbreviation <i>STP</i> or <i>STAP</i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_of_matter"" title=""State of matter"">state of matter</a>"|"
The condition of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#matter""><span title=""See entry on this page at § matter"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">matter</span></a> existing in a distinct, homogeneous, macroscopic form. <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Solid</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquid</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#gas""><span title=""See entry on this page at § gas"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gas</span></a>, and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#plasma""><span title=""See entry on this page at § plasma"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">plasma</span></a> are the four traditional states of matter and the most well-known. See also <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#phase""><span title=""See entry on this page at § phase"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">phase</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stepwise_reaction"" title=""Stepwise reaction"">stepwise reaction</a>"|"

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stereoisomer"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Stereoisomer"">stereoisomer</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>spatial isomer</b>.</span></p>
An <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#isomer""><span title=""See entry on this page at § isomer"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">isomer</span></a> which possesses an identical <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_composition""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical composition"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical composition</span></a> but which differs in the spatial arrangement of its atoms.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stoichiometry"" title=""Stoichiometry"">stoichiometry</a>"|"
The calculation of quantities of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#reactant""><span title=""See entry on this page at § reactant"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">reactants</span></a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#product""><span title=""See entry on this page at § product"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">products</span></a> in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical reaction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical reactions</span></a>. Stoichiometry is based on the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#law_of_conservation_of_mass""><span title=""See entry on this page at § law of conservation of mass"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">law of conservation of mass</span></a> and the observation that quantities of reactants and products typically exist in ratios of positive integers, implying that if the amounts of the separate reactants are known, then the amounts of the products can be calculated.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strong_acid"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Strong acid"">strong acid</a>"|"

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Structural_isomer"" title=""Structural isomer"">structural isomer</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>constitutional isomer</b>.</span></p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subatomic_particle"" title=""Subatomic particle"">subatomic particle</a>"|"
Any particle that is smaller than an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atom""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atom</span></a>. Examples include <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#proton""><span title=""See entry on this page at § proton"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">protons</span></a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#neutron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § neutron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">neutrons</span></a>, and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electrons</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sublimation_(chemistry)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Sublimation (chemistry)"">sublimation</a>"|"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#phase_transition""><span title=""See entry on this page at § phase transition"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">phase transition</span></a> of a substance from a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solid</span></a> to a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Limewater"" title=""Limewater"">limewater</a> fuel or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#gas""><span title=""See entry on this page at § gas"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gas</span></a> without an apparent intervening transition to a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquid</span></a> in the process.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_substance"" title=""Chemical substance"">substance</a>"|"
See <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_substance""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical substance"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical substance</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Substituent"" title=""Substituent"">substituent</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
