"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suspension_(chemistry)"" title=""Suspension (chemistry)"">suspension</a>"|"
A heterogeneous <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mixture""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mixture"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mixture</span></a> that contains <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solid</span></a> particles which are sufficiently large for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sedimentation"" title=""Sedimentation"">sedimentation</a> to occur, by which such particles separate from and settle out of the fluid over time if left undisturbed. In a suspension, the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solute""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solute"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solute</span></a> does not <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#dissolution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § dissolution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">dissolve</span></a> but remains <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#dispersion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § dispersion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">dispersed</span></a> or suspended throughout the fluid <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solvent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solvent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solvent</span></a> only transiently and with mechanical agitation. Contrast <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#colloid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § colloid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">colloid</span></a></i> and <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solution</span></a></i>."
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tarnish"" title=""Tarnish"">tarnish</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temperature"" title=""Temperature"">temperature</a>"|"
A proportional measure of the average <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#kinetic_energy""><span title=""See entry on this page at § kinetic energy"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">kinetic energy</span></a> of the random motions of the constituent microscopic particles of a system. The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#sI""><span title=""See entry on this page at § SI"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">SI</span></a> base unit for temperature is the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#kelvin""><span title=""See entry on this page at § kelvin"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">kelvin</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yield_(chemistry)"" title=""Yield (chemistry)"">theoretical yield</a>"|"
See <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#yield""><span title=""See entry on this page at § yield"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">yield</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thermal_conductivity"" title=""Thermal conductivity"">thermal conductivity</a>"|"
The property of a material that allows it to conduct thermal energy or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#heat""><span title=""See entry on this page at § heat"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">heat</span></a> (a quantity often denoted by <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle k}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>k</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle k}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c3c9a2c7b599b37105512c5d570edc034056dd40"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.211ex; height:2.176ex;"" alt=""k""/></span>).
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thermochemistry"" title=""Thermochemistry"">thermochemistry</a>"|"
The study of the absorption or release of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#heat""><span title=""See entry on this page at § heat"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">heat</span></a> during a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical reaction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical reaction</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thermodynamics"" title=""Thermodynamics"">thermodynamics</a>"|"
The study of the effects of changing temperature, volume or pressure (or work, heat, and energy) on a macroscopic scale.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_stability"" title=""Chemical stability"">thermodynamic stability</a>"|"
The condition of a system being in its lowest energy state with its environment (equilibrium).
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thermometer"" title=""Thermometer"">thermometer</a>"|"
An instrument used to measure <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#temperature""><span title=""See entry on this page at § temperature"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">temperature</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Titration"" title=""Titration"">titration</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>titrimetry</b> or <b>volumetric analysis</b>.</span></p>
A laboratory method of quantitative chemical analysis that is used to determine the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#concentration""><span title=""See entry on this page at § concentration"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">concentration</span></a> of an identified <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#analyte""><span title=""See entry on this page at § analyte"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">analyte</span></a>. The procedure involves preparing a particular <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#reagent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § reagent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">reagent</span></a> as a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#standard_solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § standard solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">standard solution</span></a> of known concentration and volume (called the <i>titrant</i> or <i>titrator</i>) and allowing it to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical reaction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">react</span></a> with a solution of the analyte (called the <i>titrand</i>) to determine the latter's concentration.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Torr"" title=""Torr"">torr</a>"|"
A unit for measuring <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#pressure""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pressure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pressure</span></a>, equivalent to 133.322 <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit)"" title=""Pascal (unit)"">Pa</a> or 1.3158×10<sup>−3</sup> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atmosphere_(unit)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Atmosphere (unit)"">atm</a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transition_metal"" title=""Transition metal"">transition metal</a>"|"
An <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#element""><span title=""See entry on this page at § element"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">element</span></a> whose atoms naturally occur with incompletely filled ""d"" sub-shells. These elements are grouped as the so-called <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#d-block""><span title=""See entry on this page at § d-block"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">d-block elements</span></a></i> in the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#periodic_table""><span title=""See entry on this page at § periodic table"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">periodic table</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transuranic_element"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Transuranic element"">transuranic element</a>"|"
Any element with an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atomic_number""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atomic number"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atomic number</span></a> greater than 92 (i.e. occurring after <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uranium"" title=""Uranium"">uranium</a> in the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#periodic_table""><span title=""See entry on this page at § periodic table"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">periodic table</span></a>). None of the transuranic elements are stable in natural conditions.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multiple_bond"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Multiple bond"">triple bond</a>"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bond</span></a> that involves the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#covalent_bond""><span title=""See entry on this page at § covalent bond"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">covalent</span></a> sharing of three <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron_pair""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron pair"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pairs of electrons</span></a> (for example, the diatomic nitrogen molecule, N<sub>2</sub>, is composed of two nitrogen atoms linked by a triple bond).
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Triple_point"" title=""Triple point"">triple point</a>"|"
The place where <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#temperature""><span title=""See entry on this page at § temperature"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">temperature</span></a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#pressure""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pressure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pressure</span></a> of three <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phase_(matter)"" title=""Phase (matter)"">phases</a> are the same. <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_(molecule)#Triple_point"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Water (molecule)"">Water</a> has a special phase diagram.
<div class=""thumb tright""><div class=""thumbinner"" style=""width:222px;""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Phase-diag2.svg"" class=""image""><img alt="""" src=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Phase-diag2.svg/220px-Phase-diag2.svg.png"" decoding=""async"" width=""220"" height=""184"" class=""thumbimage"" srcset=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Phase-diag2.svg/330px-Phase-diag2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Phase-diag2.svg/440px-Phase-diag2.svg.png 2x"" data-file-width=""530"" data-file-height=""443"" /></a>  <div class=""thumbcaption""><div class=""magnify""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Phase-diag2.svg"" class=""internal"" title=""Enlarge""></a></div>A phase diagram showing the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#triple_point""><span title=""See entry on this page at § triple point"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">triple point</span></a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#critical_point""><span title=""See entry on this page at § critical point"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">critical point</span></a> of a substance</div></div></div>"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tyndall_effect"" title=""Tyndall effect"">Tyndall effect</a>"|"
The effect of light scattering by <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#colloid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § colloid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">colloidal</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#suspension""><span title=""See entry on this page at § suspension"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">suspended</span></a> particles."
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UN_number"" title=""UN number"">UN number</a>"|"
A four-digit code used to note hazardous and flammable substances.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uncertainty"" title=""Uncertainty"">uncertainty</a>"|"
The notion that any measurement that involves estimation of any amount cannot be exactly reproducible.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uncertainty_principle"" title=""Uncertainty principle"">uncertainty principle</a>"|"
Knowing the location of a particle makes the momentum uncertain, while knowing the momentum of a particle makes the location uncertain.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_atomic_mass_unit"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Unified atomic mass unit"">unified atomic mass unit</a> (u)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>Dalton</b> (<b>Da</b>).</span></p>
A unit of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mass""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mass"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mass</span></a> approximately equal to the mass of one <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#proton""><span title=""See entry on this page at § proton"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">proton</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#neutron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § neutron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">neutron</span></a>. It is sometimes equated with the technically distinct and obsolete <i>atomic mass unit</i> and abbreviated <i>amu</i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crystal_structure"" title=""Crystal structure"">unit cell</a>"|"
The smallest repeating unit of a crystalline <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#lattice""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lattice"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lattice</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Units_conversion_by_factor-label"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Units conversion by factor-label"">unit factor</a>"|"
Statements used in converting between units.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unpaired_electron"" title=""Unpaired electron"">unpaired electron</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vacuum_flask"" title=""Vacuum flask"">vacuum flask</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>Dewar flask</b> or <b>thermos</b>.</span></p>
A storage vessel consisting of two <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#flask""><span title=""See entry on this page at § flask"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">flasks</span></a> or other containers, placed one within the other and joined at the neck, and a space in between that is partially evacuated of air, creating a near-<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vacuum"" title=""Vacuum"">vacuum</a> that significantly reduces the transfer of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#heat""><span title=""See entry on this page at § heat"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">heat</span></a> between the vessel's interior and its ambient environment. Vacuum flasks can greatly lengthen the time over which their contents remain warmer or cooler than the ambient environment.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valence_electron"" title=""Valence electron"">valence electron</a>"|"
Any of the outermost <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electrons</span></a> of an atom, which are located in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron_shell""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron shell"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electron shells</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valence_bond_theory"" title=""Valence bond theory"">valence bond theory</a>"|"
A theory explaining the chemical bonding within molecules by discussing <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valence_(chemistry)"" title=""Valence (chemistry)"">valencies</a>, the number of chemical bonds formed by an atom.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valence_(chemistry)"" title=""Valence (chemistry)"">valency</a>"|"
The combining capacity of an element.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Van_der_Waals_force"" title=""Van der Waals force"">van der Waals force</a>"|"
One of the forces (attraction/repulsion) between molecules.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Van_%27t_Hoff_factor"" title=""Van &#39;t Hoff factor"">van 't Hoff factor</a>"|"
The ratio of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mole""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mole"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">moles</span></a> of particles in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solution</span></a> to moles of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solute""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solute"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solute</span></a> dissolved.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vapor"" title=""Vapor"">vapor</a>"|"
When a substance is below the critical temperature while in the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#gas""><span title=""See entry on this page at § gas"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gas</span></a> phase.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vapor_pressure"" title=""Vapor pressure"">vapor pressure</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>equilibrium vapor pressure</b>.</span></p>
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#pressure""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pressure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pressure</span></a> exerted by a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#vapor""><span title=""See entry on this page at § vapor"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">vapor</span></a> which is in thermodynamic equilibrium with its condensed phases (<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solid</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquid</span></a>) at a given temperature in a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#closed_system""><span title=""See entry on this page at § closed system"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">closed system</span></a>. It is commonly described as the tendency of particles to spontaneously escape from the liquid or solid state into the gaseous state and is used as an indication of a liquid's <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#evaporation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § evaporation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">evaporation</span></a> rate.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vaporization"" title=""Vaporization"">vaporization</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>boiling</b>.</span></p>
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#phase_transition""><span title=""See entry on this page at § phase transition"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">phase transition</span></a> of a substance from a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquid</span></a> to a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#gas""><span title=""See entry on this page at § gas"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gas</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viscosity"" title=""Viscosity"">viscosity</a>"|"
A measure of the resistance of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquid</span></a> to flow.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volatility_(chemistry)"" title=""Volatility (chemistry)"">volatility</a>"|"
A material quality which describes how readily a substance <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#vaporization""><span title=""See entry on this page at § vaporization"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">vaporizes</span></a>. At a given temperature and pressure, a substance with high volatility is more likely to exist as a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#gas""><span title=""See entry on this page at § gas"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gas</span></a>, while a substance with low volatility is more likely to exist as a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquid</span></a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solid</span></a>; equivalently, less volatile substances will more readily <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#condensation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § condensation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">condense</span></a> from a gaseous state than highly volatile ones.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volt"" title=""Volt"">volt</a> (V)"|"
A derived unit of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electric_potential"" title=""Electric potential"">electric potential</a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electric_potential_difference"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Electric potential difference"">electric potential difference</a>, and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electromotive_force""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electromotive force"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electromotive force</span></a>, defined as one <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#joule""><span title=""See entry on this page at § joule"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">joule</span></a> of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#mechanical_work""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mechanical work"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">work</span></a> per <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#coulomb""><span title=""See entry on this page at § coulomb"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">coulomb</span></a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voltmeter"" title=""Voltmeter"">voltmeter</a>"|"
An instrument that measures electrical <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrode_potential"" title=""Electrode potential"">cell potential</a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volume"" title=""Volume"">volume</a>"|"
The quantity of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Three-dimensional_space"" title=""Three-dimensional space"">three-dimensional space</a> enclosed by a closed surface, or the space that a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_substance""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical substance"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">substance</span></a> (solid, liquid, gas, or plasma) or shape occupies or contains. The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#sI""><span title=""See entry on this page at § SI"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">SI</span></a> unit for volume is the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cubic_metre"" title=""Cubic metre"">cubic metre</a> (m<sup>3</sup>).
"
"volumetric analysis"|"
See <i><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#titration""><span title=""See entry on this page at § titration"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">titration</span></a></i>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volumetric_flask"" title=""Volumetric flask"">volumetric flask</a>"|"

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Watch_glass"" title=""Watch glass"">watch glass</a>"|"
A circular, concave piece of glass commonly used in chemistry laboratories as a working surface for various purposes, such as evaporating liquids, holding solids while they are being weighed, heating small amounts of a substance, or as a cover for a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#beaker""><span title=""See entry on this page at § beaker"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">beaker</span></a>./dd>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_(molecule)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Water (molecule)"">water</a>"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#polar""><span title=""See entry on this page at § polar"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">polar</span></a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#inorganic_compound""><span title=""See entry on this page at § inorganic compound"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">inorganic compound</span></a> with the chemical formula H<sub>2</sub>O that is a tasteless, odorless, and generally colorless <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#liquid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § liquid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">liquid</span></a> at <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#standard_temperature_and_pressure""><span title=""See entry on this page at § standard temperature and pressure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">standard temperature and pressure</span></a>, though it also occurs naturally as a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solid""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solid"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solid</span></a> and a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#gas""><span title=""See entry on this page at § gas"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gas</span></a> at the Earth's surface. It is the most abundant substance on Earth and therefore an integral component of virtually all chemical and biological systems. Water is often described as the ""universal <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#solvent""><span title=""See entry on this page at § solvent"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">solvent</span></a>"" for its inherent ability to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#dissolution""><span title=""See entry on this page at § dissolution"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">dissolve</span></a> many substances.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wave_function"" title=""Wave function"">wave function</a>"|"
A mathematical function describing the position of an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#electron""><span title=""See entry on this page at § electron"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">electron</span></a> in a three-dimensional space.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weak_acid"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Weak acid"">weak acid</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>

"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weak_base"" title=""Weak base"">weak base</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>
<p>Looks like this term doesn't have a definition yet.</p>
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wet_chemistry"" title=""Wet chemistry"">wet chemistry</a>"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also <b>bench chemistry</b> or <b>classical chemistry</b>.</span></p>
A form of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#analytical_chemistry""><span title=""See entry on this page at § analytical chemistry"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">analytical chemistry</span></a> which uses classical laboratory methods such as simple observation and elementary chemical tests to study chemicals and chemical reactions, i.e. without the use of sophisticated instruments or automated or computerized analysis. It is often used in schools to teach the principles of chemistry to students.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mechanical_work"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Mechanical work"">work</a>"|"
<p>Maybe consider making a contribution to this <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Chemistry-Terms-Flashcards"">project</a> or even better improve the original Wikipedia article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms"">""Glossary of chemistry terms""</a> by making a contribution and <a href=""https://twitter.com/darigovresearch"">let us know</a>!</p>

"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Work-up_(chemistry)"" title=""Work-up (chemistry)"">work-up</a>"|"
The series of manipulations required to isolate and purify the desired <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#product""><span title=""See entry on this page at § product"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">product</span></a> or products of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical reaction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical reaction</span></a>."
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/X-ray"" title=""X-ray"">X-ray</a>"|"
A form of ionizing, electromagnetic radiation between <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamma_rays"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Gamma rays"">gamma</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultraviolet"" title=""Ultraviolet"">UV</a> rays in the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromagnetic_spectrum"" title=""Electromagnetic spectrum"">electromagnetic spectrum</a>.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/X-ray_scattering_techniques"" title=""X-ray scattering techniques"">X-ray diffraction</a>"|"
a method for establishing structures of <i>crystalline</i> solids using single wavelength X-rays and looking at diffraction pattern.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/X-ray_photoelectron_spectroscopy"" title=""X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy"">X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy</a>"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#spectroscopy""><span title=""See entry on this page at § spectroscopy"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">spectroscopic</span></a> technique used to measure the composition of a material."
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yield_(chemistry)"" title=""Yield (chemistry)"">yield</a>"|"
The quantifiable amount of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#product""><span title=""See entry on this page at § product"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">product</span></a> produced during a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#chemical_reaction""><span title=""See entry on this page at § chemical reaction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical reaction</span></a>."
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zone_melting"" title=""Zone melting"">zone melting</a>"|"
A way to remove impurities from an element by melting it and slowly travel down an ingot (cast).
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zwitterion"" title=""Zwitterion"">zwitterion</a>"|"
A chemical compound whose net charge is zero and hence is electrically neutral. But there are some positive and negative charges in it, due to the formal charge, owing to the partial charges of its constituent atoms.
"
"<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zinc"" title=""Zinc"">zinc</a>"|"
A metallic <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#element""><span title=""See entry on this page at § element"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">chemical element</span></a> with <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atomic_number""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atomic number"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">atomic number</span></a> 30 and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_chemistry_terms#atomic_symbol""><span title=""See entry on this page at § atomic symbol"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">symbol</span></a> Zn.
"
